# 1. GaN-on-SiæŠ€æœ¯åœ¨æ¯«ç±³æ³¢çš„åº”ç”¨_è¥¿å®‰ç”µå­ç§‘æŠ€å¤§å­¦_åˆ˜å¿—å®æ•™æˆ

ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“ä¸»è¦æŠ€æœ¯æŒ‘æˆ˜

- çƒ­å…¼å®¹æ€§é—®é¢˜ï¼šæ°®åŒ–é•“å¾®æ³¢æ¯«ç±³æ³¢ç”µè·¯ï¼Œå‘çƒ­æ¯”è¾ƒä¸¥é‡ï¼Œä¼šå¼•èµ·å‘¨å›´Si-CMOSå™¨ä»¶çš„é˜ˆå€¼ç”µå‹æ¼‚ç§»ã€æ¼ç”µå¢å¤§ç­‰é—®é¢˜
- ç”µç£å…¼å®¹æ€§é—®é¢˜ï¼šæ°®åŒ–é•“ç”µè·¯å·¥ä½œæ—¶çš„åå‹æ¯”è¾ƒå¤§ï¼Œç”µåœºè€¦åˆåˆ°CMOSåŒºåŸŸï¼›å°„é¢‘ç”µè·¯å·¥ä½œæ—¶çš„ç”µç£åœºåˆ†å¸ƒæ•ˆåº”ã€ç”µç£æ³¢è¾å°„
- å·¥è‰ºå…¼å®¹æ€§é—®é¢˜ï¼šæ°®åŒ–é•“å™¨ä»¶åˆ¶å¤‡æ—¶çš„å·¥è‰ºæ¡ä»¶ï¼ŒåŒ…æ‹¬é‡‘å±ã€æ¸©åº¦ã€åº”åŠ›ç­‰å¯¹SiCMOSçš„å™¨ä»¶æ€§èƒ½çš„è¯¦ç»†å½±å“

# 2.IRDSå…³äºGaNå™¨ä»¶å’Œè¡¬åº•çš„åˆ†æ 2022IRDS_WP-MtM

## 2.1 GaNå™¨ä»¶å’Œè¡¬åº•ç»¼è¿°

3.3.2. GAN-DEVICES AND SUBSTRATES

GaN semiconductor devices provide competitive system advantage in terms of thermal performance, efficiency, weight and size. GaN is anticipated to be the next generation power semiconductor and thus different countries are indulged in developing widespread applications of GaN semiconductors. The wide bandgap semiconductor technology has matured rapidly over several years. In fact, gallium nitride high electron mobility transistors (GaN HEMTs) have been available as commercial off-the-shelf devices since 2005. Well-known GaN device manufacturers are Infineon, NXP, ON Semiconductor, STMicroelectronics, EPC, Texas Instruments, Transphorm, Navitas, GaNSystems, Nexperia, TSMC,Sumitomo, Exagan, Innoscience, Power Integrations and Sanken.
Substrate Diameterâ€”Today, 6â€ to 8â€ wafer size, low vertical leakage current, current collapse free GaN-on-Si wafers are available on the open market. This remarkable achievement is a result of concentrated epi efforts during the past years that led to an ever-increasing understanding of the physical/technical properties of GaN-on-Si growth and corresponding improvements. Pricing for such material has come down significantly in the recent years. It is generally agreed that the magic cost target of 1.5 $/cm2 for epitaxial material, which is also the price point at which GaN technology becomes cost-competitive with Si-based components at the device-level, can be achieved within the next couple of years under the important assumption that the wafers can be produced in volume. A next logical evolution would be to make the transition to 300 mm wafer diameters (as demonstrated for RF power GaN-Devices by Intel), but it is as yet an open question whether this makes sense from an economical perspective.
Voltage Ratingâ€”Standard products of GaN-on-Si typically feature an epilayer thickness of 4 Âµm to 6 Âµm, yielding a voltage handling capability of 650 V, including derating for temperature and lack of avalanche capability. Recent literature reports on boosted voltage rating of epi-wafers to values beyond 1200 V at room temperature by improvements in epitaxial recipes as well as increased layer thickness. However, due to the high intrinsic strain in GaN-on-Si layer stacks as well as the drive towards the adoption of semi standard substrate thicknesses, there is a fundamental limit to the maximal thickness (and breakdown voltage) that can be achieved. One possible way to increase the voltage rating of GaN-on-Si devices is the removal and replacement of the substrate, although questions concerning manufacturability and reliability of such an approach remain. On the other hand, for higher breakdown voltages the chip area utilization and the fact that large electric fields have to be handled on top of the active device becomes more and more problematic. True vertical GaN devices where the off-state voltage is block over an n--doped vertical drift region become increasinglyimportant.

Lateral device architectureâ€”Usually lateral devices embed a pGaN gate architecture or use a cascode topology to achieve n-Off behavior. Recently studies have shown the potential of MOS gate on GaN with oxide such as Al2O3 or SiO2 to achieve a stable n-Off behavior. This novel gate architecture is expected to increase the reliability of the overall transistor by the reduction of the gate leakage. Nevertheless this technology requires a highly stable and well-engineered oxide/GaN interface as well as a high quality oxide with limited trapping to ensure a stable Vth of the transistor during operation. Local substrate removal, introduced by Imec and CNRS Lille, also are a valuable solution to increase the lateral breakdown beyond 2 kV.

Transport propertiesâ€”The hetero-structures are typically based on AlGaN barrier material and have a sheet resistance of around 300 Î©/sq is obtained (which directly influences the deviceâ€™s on-state resistance) with SiN/GaN/AlGaN/AlN/GaN structure.13
Vertical Devicesâ€”Besides lateral devices, also vertical devices are being investigated. They hold the promise of higher attainable power densities as well as avalanche capability. Although the structure does not have the advantage of electron transport along the two-dimensional electron gas (2DEG), the high channel mobility of the MOS channel provides a better Ron Ã— A than other WBSs in the breakdown voltage range from 600 V to 1.5 kV. The vertical current flow makes this type of device more sensitive to (vertical) threading dislocations. Therefore, this technology requires a high-quality GaN substrate and innovative and optimized growth technology on it. The quality of GaN substrates for these applications is also improving. Although not yet in practical use, manufacturing process technologies, such as low doping epitaxial growth, Mg ion implantation, and low damage etching, have been developed to a more advanced level. However, the major problem of reducing wafer cost still remains. In MOS-based devices, the choice of the insulator and the processes to control the trapped charges is still under debate. Many device concepts are currently competing against each other, in this connection vertical FinFETs should be mentioned. They do not need any p-type doped epitaxial layer and rely on electron accumulation at the gate insulator /semiconductor interface. Due to the absence of a p-type doping they do not show any reverse recovery effects and therefore outperform most of the other vertical device concepts. There are some 
literature reports about the development of GaN superjunction devices with superior performance. However, the practical implementation is to date troubled by issues, e.g., to perform the trench regrowth of p-type GaN.

Development of GaN substratesâ€”Upgrading the quality of GaN substrates has been a major challenge for vertical GaN power devices. Mainstream of the fabrication method of GaN substrates is thick GaN growth on sapphire using highspeed HVPE method, which has adequate buffer layer to remove GaN from sapphire. Though the method is conventional, the quality of the GaN substrate is drastically improved recently. A dislocation density in the mid 105 cm-2 range was obtained with HVPE grown GaN on sapphire or ammonothermal-bulk GaN substrates. Moreover, to reduce the dislocation density, combinations of ammonothermal method or sodium flux method with HVPE method are being developed. With this method, the dislocation density can be reduced by one or two orders of magnitude compared with conventional high-quality GaN substrates. The developed wafer size is also expanding from 2â€ to 6â€. However, as main market of the GaN substrate at present time is optical devices (LEDs and lasers), needs for large size substrates is still small. When large devices such as power devices become mainstream, the substrate costs will become lower. However, the breakthroughs for drastically cost down are still required, which are, for example, slice technologies of bulk GaN and wafer bonding to backing plates. 

On-chip integrationâ€”A further path to cost reduction for GaN technology is to include several components on a single chip, allowing to save component, packaging and design costs for creating a full system. Beyond merely costs advantages, a monolithic integration will also enable the main potential of GaN to be tapped, which is a high commutation speed, leading to an increased switching frequency for the power circuit. Discrete Si power components can be quite readily integrated in a power circuit; however, GaN components can deliver high power at a fast switching frequency. These properties lead to a stringent requirement on the design of circuit and interconnect parasitic. Integrating, for example, two switches on a single die can also significantly reduce interconnect parasitic, offering further system-level performance benefits.

GaN è¡¬åº•çš„å¼€å‘â€”â€”æé«˜ GaN è¡¬åº•çš„è´¨é‡ä¸€ç›´æ˜¯å‚ç›´ GaN åŠŸç‡å™¨ä»¶é¢ä¸´çš„ä¸»è¦æŒ‘æˆ˜ã€‚GaN è¡¬åº•çš„ä¸»æµåˆ¶é€ æ–¹æ³•æ˜¯ä½¿ç”¨é«˜é€Ÿ HVPE æ³•åœ¨è“å®çŸ³ä¸Šç”Ÿé•¿åš GaNï¼Œè¯¥æ–¹æ³•å…·æœ‰è¶³å¤Ÿçš„ç¼“å†²å±‚ä»¥ä»è“å®çŸ³ä¸­å»é™¤ GaNã€‚è™½ç„¶è¯¥æ–¹æ³•æ˜¯å¸¸è§„æ–¹æ³•ï¼Œä½† GaN è¡¬åº•çš„è´¨é‡æœ€è¿‘å¾—åˆ°äº†å¤§å¹…æ”¹å–„ã€‚ä½¿ç”¨ HVPE åœ¨è“å®çŸ³ä¸Šç”Ÿé•¿çš„ GaN æˆ–æ°¨çƒ­å—çŠ¶ GaN è¡¬åº•å¯è·å¾— 105 cm-2 ä¸­ç­‰èŒƒå›´çš„ä½é”™å¯†åº¦ã€‚æ­¤å¤–ï¼Œä¸ºäº†é™ä½ä½é”™å¯†åº¦ï¼Œæ­£åœ¨å¼€å‘æ°¨çƒ­æ³•æˆ–é’ ç†”å‰‚æ³•ä¸ HVPE æ–¹æ³•çš„ç»„åˆã€‚ä¸ä¼ ç»Ÿçš„é«˜è´¨é‡ GaN è¡¬åº•ç›¸æ¯”ï¼Œä½¿ç”¨è¿™ç§æ–¹æ³•å¯ä»¥å°†ä½é”™å¯†åº¦é™ä½ä¸€åˆ°ä¸¤ä¸ªæ•°é‡çº§ã€‚å¼€å‘çš„æ™¶åœ†å°ºå¯¸ä¹Ÿä» 2 è‹±å¯¸æ‰©å¤§åˆ° 6 è‹±å¯¸ã€‚ä½†æ˜¯ï¼Œç”±äºç›®å‰ GaN è¡¬åº•çš„ä¸»è¦å¸‚åœºæ˜¯å…‰å­¦å™¨ä»¶ï¼ˆLED å’Œæ¿€å…‰å™¨ï¼‰ï¼Œå› æ­¤å¯¹å¤§å°ºå¯¸è¡¬åº•çš„éœ€æ±‚ä»ç„¶å¾ˆå°ã€‚å½“å¤§å‹å™¨ä»¶ï¼ˆå¦‚åŠŸç‡å™¨ä»¶ï¼‰æˆä¸ºä¸»æµæ—¶ï¼ŒåŸºæ¿æˆæœ¬å°†ä¼šé™ä½ã€‚ç„¶è€Œï¼Œå¤§å¹…é™ä½æˆæœ¬ä»éœ€çªç ´ï¼Œä¾‹å¦‚å—çŠ¶ GaN çš„åˆ‡ç‰‡æŠ€æœ¯å’Œæ™¶åœ†ä¸èƒŒæ¿çš„é”®åˆã€‚

ç‰‡ä¸Šé›†æˆâ€”â€”é™ä½ GaN æŠ€æœ¯æˆæœ¬çš„å¦ä¸€ç§æ–¹æ³•æ˜¯å°†å¤šä¸ªç»„ä»¶é›†æˆåœ¨å•ä¸ªèŠ¯ç‰‡ä¸Šï¼Œä»è€ŒèŠ‚çœç»„ä»¶ã€å°è£…å’Œè®¾è®¡æˆæœ¬ï¼Œä»¥åˆ›å»ºå®Œæ•´çš„ç³»ç»Ÿã€‚é™¤äº†æˆæœ¬ä¼˜åŠ¿ä¹‹å¤–ï¼Œå•ç‰‡é›†æˆè¿˜å°†èƒ½å¤ŸæŒ–æ˜ GaN çš„ä¸»è¦æ½œåŠ›ï¼Œå³é«˜æ¢å‘é€Ÿåº¦ï¼Œä»è€Œæé«˜åŠŸç‡ç”µè·¯çš„å¼€å…³é¢‘ç‡ã€‚åˆ†ç«‹çš„ Si åŠŸç‡å…ƒä»¶å¯ä»¥å¾ˆå®¹æ˜“åœ°é›†æˆåˆ°åŠŸç‡ç”µè·¯ä¸­ï¼›ç„¶è€Œï¼ŒGaN å…ƒä»¶å¯ä»¥åœ¨å¿«é€Ÿå¼€å…³é¢‘ç‡ä¸‹æä¾›é«˜åŠŸç‡ã€‚è¿™äº›ç‰¹æ€§å¯¹ç”µè·¯å’Œäº’è¿å¯„ç”Ÿçš„è®¾è®¡æå‡ºäº†ä¸¥æ ¼çš„è¦æ±‚ã€‚ä¾‹å¦‚ï¼Œåœ¨å•ä¸ªèŠ¯ç‰‡ä¸Šé›†æˆä¸¤ä¸ªå¼€å…³ä¹Ÿå¯ä»¥æ˜¾è‘—é™ä½äº’è¿å¯„ç”Ÿï¼Œä»è€Œæä¾›è¿›ä¸€æ­¥çš„ç³»ç»Ÿçº§æ€§èƒ½ä¼˜åŠ¿ã€‚

## 2.2 2019-2025çš„å›°éš¾æŒ‘æˆ˜
**Difficult Challenges 2019-2025**

1. GaN-on-Si substrates, large diameter (8â€), low defectivity and low cost.

Potential solutions

- New generation of MOCVD reactors allow to scale to 200 mm and 300 mm
- Move from multi-wafer to single wafer reactor concept for 300 mm for better control on temperature profile across the wafer, bow and warp
- Improve substrate quality by growing on non-Si substrates (e.g., poly-AlN) and (potentially) liftoff

Strain engineering
â€¢ Growth and processing of wafers thicker than SEMI standard (Si fab 
compatibility to be solved)
â€¢ Optimized nucleation, layer-sequence, and growth processes
â€¢ Growth on CTE matched substrates (e.g., GaN-on-Si/AlN)
â€¢ Alternative approaches: GaN-on-SiC â†’ Quanfine (inexpensive semi-insulating SiC substrates required). DENSO (GaN epi-growth on 4 degree off-axis 4H-SiC without buffer layers by tri-halide vapor phase epitaxy)
â€¢ GaN-on-Sapphire

Low defectivity
â€¢ Clean Si substrates
â€¢ Optimized epi growth (crystal quality, dislocations)
â€¢ Epi tool automation
â€¢ Improved reactor cleaning processes
â€¢ Improved epi wafer cleaning processes
â€¢ Better defect detection tools. Binning capability pits vs. particles
â€¢ Enabling CL as defect (dislocation) detection tool for production monitoring
â€¢ In-line detection and monitoring of Si, C, Mg doping

Low cost
â€¢ Increased epi growth speed
â€¢ Improved break-down behavior (more V/Âµm buffer thickness)
â€¢ Shortened reactor cleaning processes (e.g., in-situ cleaning)
â€¢ Epi tool automation
â€¢ Improved tool up-times and reduction of maintenance intervals
â€¢ Less monitoring effort due to increased process stability
â€¢ Eventually GaN-on-Si in 300 mm (beyond 2025)

- ä»å¤šæ™¶åœ†è½¬å˜ä¸º 300 æ¯«ç±³å•æ™¶åœ†ååº”å™¨æ¦‚å¿µï¼Œä»¥æ›´å¥½åœ°æ§åˆ¶æ•´ä¸ªæ™¶åœ†çš„æ¸©åº¦åˆ†å¸ƒã€å¼¯æ›²å’Œç¿˜æ›²

2.GaN Devicesâ€”Low leakage, reliability, avalanche capability

Potential solutions

Low buffer leakage through improved substrate quality
Reduction in gate leakage by Schottky gate engineering or by adopting an alternative regrowth of the gate after recess
Better reliability by improved UID and barrier quality (less defects, better doping control). Improve hot carrier injection by improving quantum well
Low leakage
â€¢ Reduced dislocation density in GaN epi
â€¢ pGaN devicesâ€”gate module engineering, Schottky type vs. ohmic gate 
contact
Reliability, incl. dynamic properties
â€¢ Electric field management
â€¢ Reduced dislocation and defect density
â€¢ Optimized buffer trapping
â€¢ Improved passivation processes and materials (e.g., atomic layer deposition)
â€¢ Improved GaN purity (in particular in unintentionally doped GaN channel)
â€¢ Engineering of hole injection for trapped charge compensation
â€¢ Resistivity balance in layer stack
â€¢ TCAD model for buffer & device leakage, trapping, detrapping
â€¢ For p-GaN gate moduleâ€”Leakage balance between Schottky diode and pn diode

4.GaN Devicesâ€”Regrown ohmic contacts

Potential solutions

Today ohmic contact resistance is ~0.1 Î©.mm with a standard Ti/Al metal stack, which is sufficient for power devices
Silicon doping for n ohmic contacts
High temperature ion implantation techniques in combination with high temperature pulse activation need to be investigated

### 2.2.4.GaN å™¨ä»¶â€”â€”å†ç”Ÿæ¬§å§†æ¥è§¦

æ½œåœ¨è§£å†³æ–¹æ¡ˆ

ç›®å‰ï¼Œé‡‡ç”¨æ ‡å‡† Ti/Al é‡‘å±å †æ ˆçš„æ¬§å§†æ¥è§¦ç”µé˜»çº¦ä¸º 0.1 Î©.mmï¼Œè¿™å¯¹äºåŠŸç‡å™¨ä»¶æ¥è¯´å·²ç»è¶³å¤Ÿäº†
n æ¬§å§†æ¥è§¦çš„ç¡…æºæ‚
éœ€è¦ç ”ç©¶é«˜æ¸©ç¦»å­æ³¨å…¥æŠ€æœ¯ä¸é«˜æ¸©è„‰å†²æ¿€æ´»ç›¸ç»“åˆ

5.GaN Devicesâ€”On-Chip Integration 

pMOS device that is compatible with the standard HEMT process flow
Creation of a 2DHG based devices. Some studies showing the potentiality of AlN/GaN Barrier to create such a channel

6.GaN modules 

Parallellization of several GaN die in a module
Co-integration of the driver (and controller ?)
Simulation approach to optimize parasitic inductance (â€œdigital twinâ€)
Monolithic GaN driver integration wherever necessary and of advantage. This needs to be aligned with the hybrid GaN die integration capabilities.

7.High power switching of GaN devices with high reliability

Epi without trapping effects to decrease hot electrons tapping during Hard Switching operation which limits the SSOA of commercially available devices

8.GaN Multi MHz operation @ 100 W and more

Decrease as much as possible the internal parasitic capacitance as well as the dynamic Ron of the transistors operated in a multi-MHZ switching mode

9.Channel conduction in 4H-SiC trench-MOSFETs

Alternative approaches to standard nitridation (e.g., post-oxidation processes and implants)

10.Ohmic contacts on p-type 4H-SiC for body-diode and bipolar devices

Alternative solutions (Ti- or Al-based) to the standard nickel silicide

11.4H-SiC devices on 8-inches substrates 

Development of equipment able to guarantee processes uniformity (high-temperature annealing, implantation, oxidation). Low wafer cost of $800 (8-inch)

12.Development of cubic polytype (3C-SiC) for 600-900 V devices

Compliant substrates to reduce the defect density of 3C-SiC on Si substrates

13.Ga2O3 melt bulk growth 

Increasing Ga2O3 bulk and wafers in size to 6â€-diameter and beyond

14.Ga2O3 epitaxial thin-film growth 

For HVPE and MOCVD:
- Precise control of background donor density
- Deep-acceptor doping
Heterostructures

15.Ga2O3 Schottky barrier diodes 

Enhancement of breakdown voltage with keeping a reasonable on-resistance
Reliability and endurance test

16.Ga2O3 transistors 

Development of device architectures
Development of fundamental device process technologies

### 2.2.15. Ga2O3 è‚–ç‰¹åŸºåŠ¿å’äºŒæç®¡

### 2.2.16. Ga2O3 æ™¶ä½“ç®¡

å™¨ä»¶æ¶æ„å¼€å‘
åŸºæœ¬å™¨ä»¶å·¥è‰ºæŠ€æœ¯çš„å¼€å‘

**Difficult Challenges 2025-2034 Potential solutions**

1.Move to 300 mm 

Single wafer MOCVD reactor

2.GaN automotive qualification 

Guarantee low ppb levels
Need good epitaxy

3.GaN Smart power 

Requires all elements from monolithic GaN.
Cost reduction of GaN wafers to take benefit of an all-GaN technology. However, a well-adapted combination between Si logic devices and GaN power switching devices should be feasible as well. This approach allows combining the advantages of both worlds.

4.Development of device process on 3C-SiC 

Adapting the main processes used for 4H-SiC devices, special challenge in implanted dopant activation.

5.III-Nitrides growth on arbitrary substrates 

Use of 2D materials with hexagonal structure (graphene, MoS2 or h-BN) as compliant interlayer for quasi-van der Waals growth of III-N.

6.Improved thermal management of GaN power HEMTs

Use of high thermal conductivity graphene structures as heat sinks for localized heat dissipation in high power GaN HEMTs.

7.Monolithic integration HS/LS 

Potential solutions for resolving cross-talk and back-gating effects (electrical isolation of HS/LS and backside):
- Junction isolation;
- GaN-on-SOI;
- GaN-on-other insulating substrates.

8.On-Chip Integration 

â€¢ Homogeneous integration of driver, control, and protection functions by using GaN process design kit
â€¢ Realization of device library based on pure GaN technology
â€¢ Realization of true p channel devices with acceptable mobility
â€¢ Heterogeneous integration of silicon and GaN technology
â€¢ Chip bonding or wafer bonding as conceivable options

9.Revolutionary shrink path 
â€¢ Three-dimensional gate structures
â€¢ FIN-FET devices
â€¢ Nano-structured gates ( e.g., Tri-Gates)
â€¢ Multi-channel devices

10.Vertical devices 
Development of large area (150mm) GaN bulk substrates with high conductivity (e.g., 0.02 ï—cm) at a reasonable price (e.g., 1500$)

11.GaN superjunction devices 
Simulations show that the specific on-resistance of vertical superjunction devices are 10x and 1000x lower than 2H-GaN 1D limit with breakdown voltage 1kV and 10kV, respectively (Refâ€”Xiang Zhou et al, Compound Semiconductor week 2019)

12.Vertical Ga2O3 Schottky barrier diodes and transistors

Starting developments on vertical Ga2O3 devices in industry, together with academia

æ— è®ºæ˜¯åˆ¶é€ æµ‹è¯•å¤±è´¥è¿˜æ˜¯ç°åœºé€€è´§ï¼Œç¡®å®šæœ‰é—®é¢˜çš„å°è£…éƒ¨ä»¶çš„æ ¹æœ¬åŸå› çš„å¿…è¦æ­¥éª¤éƒ½æ˜¯ä»æ•…éšœéš”ç¦»å¼€å§‹ã€‚â€œè€ƒè™‘åˆ° GaN å¸¦éš™çš„ç›´æ¥æ€§è´¨åŠå…¶åœ¨ç”µå‹/é¢‘ç‡/åŠŸç‡å¯†åº¦æ–¹é¢çš„æ“ä½œçª—å£ï¼Œä¼ ç»Ÿçš„æ•…éšœéš”ç¦»æ–¹æ³•ï¼ˆä¾‹å¦‚å…‰å‘å°„å…‰è°±ï¼‰è¢«è¿«å…³æ³¨å…¸å‹ç”µæ°”ç¼ºé™·çš„ä¸åŒæ³¢é•¿å’Œä¸åŒæ¿€å‘èŒƒå›´ï¼Œâ€èµ›é»˜é£ä¸–å°”çš„ Mani è¯´ã€‚â€œçƒ­è½½æµå­å¯¹åªæ˜¯ä¸€ä¸ªä¾‹å­ï¼Œå®ƒå‡¸æ˜¾äº† GaN å’Œç¡…å™¨ä»¶ä¹‹é—´çš„æ ¹æœ¬åŒºåˆ«ã€‚â€

# 5.GaN å’Œ SiC åŠŸç‡å™¨ä»¶å›é¡¾ä¸å±•æœ›ï¼šå·¥ä¸šæœ€æ–°æŠ€æœ¯ã€åº”ç”¨å’Œè§‚ç‚¹

æˆ‘ä»¬å¯¹å¸‚åœºä¸Šå¯ç”¨äºå½“å‰å’Œä¸‹ä¸€ä»£ç”µåŠ›ç”µå­çš„ç¢³åŒ–ç¡… (SiC) å’Œæ°®åŒ–é•“ (GaN) æ™¶ä½“ç®¡è¿›è¡Œäº†å…¨é¢çš„å›é¡¾å’Œå±•æœ›ã€‚é¦–å…ˆè®¨è®ºäº† GaN å’Œ SiC å™¨ä»¶ä¹‹é—´çš„ææ–™ç‰¹æ€§å’Œç»“æ„å·®å¼‚ã€‚åŸºäºå¯¹ä¸åŒå•†ç”¨ GaN å’Œ SiC åŠŸç‡æ™¶ä½“ç®¡çš„åˆ†æï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬æè¿°äº†è¿™äº›æŠ€æœ¯çš„æœ€æ–°è¿›å±•ï¼Œé‡ç‚¹ä»‹ç»äº†ä¼˜å…ˆåŠŸç‡è½¬æ¢æ‹“æ‰‘å’Œæ¯ä¸ªæŠ€æœ¯å¹³å°çš„å…³é”®ç‰¹æ€§ã€‚è¿˜å›é¡¾äº† GaN å’Œ SiC å™¨ä»¶çš„å½“å‰å’Œæœªæ¥åº”ç”¨é¢†åŸŸã€‚æœ¬æ–‡è¿˜æŠ¥å‘Šäº†ä¸è¿™ä¸¤ç§æŠ€æœ¯ç›¸å…³çš„ä¸»è¦å¯é æ€§æ–¹é¢ã€‚å¯¹äº GaN HEMTï¼Œæè¿°äº†é˜ˆå€¼ç”µå‹ç¨³å®šæ€§ã€åŠ¨æ€å¯¼é€šç”µé˜»å’Œå‡»ç©¿é™åˆ¶ï¼Œè€Œå¯¹äº SiC MOSFETï¼Œåˆ†æè¿˜ä¾§é‡äºæ …ææ°§åŒ–ç‰©æ•…éšœå’ŒçŸ­è·¯ (SC) ç¨³å¥æ€§ã€‚æœ€åï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬æ¦‚è¿°äº†æ­¤ç±»ææ–™åœ¨ä¸åŒé¢†åŸŸä¸­çš„å‰æ™¯ã€‚æŒ‡å‡ºäº†è¿™ä¸¤ç§æŠ€æœ¯æœªæ¥å¯èƒ½çš„æ”¹è¿›å’Œå‘å±•ã€‚å¼ºè°ƒäº†æ··åˆè½¬æ¢å™¨çš„è¦æ±‚ï¼Œä»¥åŠå¯¹æ€§èƒ½çš„ç²¾å¿ƒä¼˜åŒ–å’Œåˆ›æ–°ä¼˜åŒ–å·¥å…·çš„ä½¿ç”¨ã€‚

5. æåŒ–æ•ˆåº”

**å°„é¢‘ (RF) çš„æ¼”å˜**
åœ¨å°„é¢‘é¢†åŸŸï¼ŒGaAs æŠ€æœ¯æ˜¯æ™ºèƒ½æ‰‹æœºå°„é¢‘å‰ç«¯æ¨¡å—çš„æˆç†Ÿæ„å»ºæ¨¡å—ï¼Œå¹¶ä¸”åœ¨æ±½è½¦åº”ç”¨é¢†åŸŸæ˜¾ç¤ºå‡ºå¢é•¿æœºä¼šã€‚å°„é¢‘ (RF) ä¸­çš„å¦ä¸€ç§å…³é”®ææ–™æ˜¯ç¢³åŒ–ç¡…ä¸Šæ°®åŒ–é•“ (GaN-on-SiC)ã€‚åœ¨è¿‡å»äºŒåå¹´ä¸­ï¼Œè¿™ç§ææ–™å·²ç”¨äºå¼€å‘å›½é˜²å’Œèˆªç©ºèˆªå¤©åº”ç”¨çš„åŠŸç‡æ”¾å¤§å™¨ï¼Œç¾å›½æ”¿åºœå¯¹æ­¤ç»™äºˆäº†å¤§åŠ›æ”¯æŒã€‚éšç€ 5G çš„å‡ºç°ï¼Œæ–°çš„å®åŸºç«™æ­£åœ¨é‡‡ç”¨ GaN æŠ€æœ¯å–ä»£ç°æœ‰çš„ç¡… LDMOSï¼Œæ­¤ä¸¾å¯åœ¨æ›´é«˜é¢‘ç‡ä¸‹ä»¥æ›´é«˜çš„æ•ˆç‡å®ç°æ›´å¤æ‚çš„æ¶æ„ã€‚å°„é¢‘ GaN æŠ€æœ¯ä¹Ÿåœ¨æ‰©å±•åˆ°å«æ˜Ÿé€šä¿¡å’Œå°„é¢‘èƒ½æºç­‰å¸‚åœºã€‚æ ¹æ®æˆ‘ä»¬æœ€è¿‘çš„åˆ†æï¼Œåˆ° 2029 å¹´ï¼Œæ•´ä¸ªå°„é¢‘ GaN å™¨ä»¶å¸‚åœºè§„æ¨¡å°†ä» 2023 å¹´çš„ 11 äº¿ç¾å…ƒå¢é•¿åˆ° 20.7 äº¿ç¾å…ƒ4,7ã€‚

è¿‘å¹´æ¥ï¼Œç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“æ˜¯ RF å™¨ä»¶çš„ä¸€ç§æ›¿ä»£ææ–™ç³»ç»Ÿï¼Œå¼•èµ·äº†äººä»¬çš„å…³æ³¨ã€‚å»å¹´ï¼Œè‹±é£å‡Œå‘ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½å¸‚åœºæ¨å‡ºäº†ä¸€ç§åœ¨ 200 æ¯«ç±³æ™¶åœ†ä¸ŠåŠ å·¥çš„ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“åŠŸç‡æ”¾å¤§å™¨æ¨¡å—ï¼Œç›´æ¥ä¸ç¢³åŒ–ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“æŠ€æœ¯ç«äº‰ã€‚ç”±äºå…·æœ‰æ‰©å±•åˆ° 300 æ¯«ç±³çš„æ½œåŠ›ï¼ŒRF ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“å¯ä»¥æä¾›æ€§èƒ½å’Œæˆæœ¬ä¼˜åŠ¿ï¼Œä¸ 6G PA çš„ GaAs æŠ€æœ¯ç«äº‰ã€‚å…¶ä»–æ¢ç´¢ RF ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“æŠ€æœ¯çš„å…¬å¸åŒ…æ‹¬ UMCã€STMicroelectronicsã€GlobalFoundriesã€Sony å’Œ Finwaveã€‚éšç€è¿™äº›æ–°æ¥è€…å¯¹åŠŸç‡ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“è¿›è¡ŒæŠ•èµ„ï¼Œä»–ä»¬èƒ½å¤Ÿä½¿ç”¨ 200 æ¯«ç±³è®¾æ–½è¿›å…¥ RF åº”ç”¨ï¼Œè€Œæ— éœ€è¿›è¡Œé£é™©æŠ•èµ„ã€‚150

æ¯«ç±³ RF ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“æŠ€æœ¯çš„å…ˆé©±æ˜¯ Macomã€‚åå¤šå¹´æ¥ï¼Œè¿™å®¶ç¾å›½èŠ¯ç‰‡åˆ¶é€ å•†ä¸€ç›´åœ¨å†›ç”¨æˆ˜æœ¯æ— çº¿ç”µè®¾è®¡ä¸­å æ®ä¸»å¯¼åœ°ä½ã€‚å»å¹´ï¼ŒMacom é€šè¿‡æ”¶è´­ Ommic SAS è¿›å†›å«æ˜Ÿé€šä¿¡é¢†åŸŸï¼Œå¹¶é€šè¿‡æ”¶è´­ Wolfspeed çš„ RF ä¸šåŠ¡å¢å¼ºäº†å…¶ GaN-on-SiC äº§å“ç»„åˆã€‚è¿™äº›æ”¶è´­ä½¿ Macom æˆä¸ºå½“ä»Šå››å¤§ RF GaN è®¾å¤‡åˆ¶é€ å•†ä¹‹ä¸€ã€‚

åœ¨è¿‡å»çš„äºŒåå¹´ä¸­ï¼Œå°„é¢‘GaNæŠ€æœ¯ä¸æ–­å‘å±•ï¼Œæœ€åˆæ‰æ ¹äºå›½é˜²åº”ç”¨ï¼Œç°åœ¨åˆ™åœ¨æ»¡è¶³ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½å’Œå«æ˜Ÿé€šä¿¡éœ€æ±‚æ–¹é¢æ¢ç´¢æ–°é¢†åŸŸã€‚éšç€ GaN-on-SiC æŠ€æœ¯çš„æˆç†Ÿï¼Œå®ƒæ­£åœ¨æˆä¸ºå„ç§åº”ç”¨çš„æ ‡å‡†ï¼Œå¹¶ç¨³æ­¥è¶…è¶Š Si LDMOS å’Œ GaAs ç­‰ç«äº‰æŠ€æœ¯ï¼Œèµ¢å¾—å¸‚åœºä»½é¢ã€‚GaN æŠ€æœ¯æ³¨é‡åŠŸç‡æ•ˆç‡ã€å¯é æ€§å’Œç©ºé—´ä¼˜åŒ–ï¼Œæ­£å˜å¾—ä¸å¯æˆ–ç¼ºã€‚ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½å¸‚åœºæ­£åœ¨è§è¯åŠŸç‡æ”¾å¤§å™¨ (PA)éœ€æ±‚çš„é‡å¤§è½¬å˜ï¼Œä¸ºè‹±é£å‡Œäº 2023 å¹´åœ¨ 8 è‹±å¯¸å¹³å°ä¸Šæ¨å‡ºçš„ GaN-on-Si æŠ€æœ¯é“ºå¹³äº†é“è·¯ã€‚è¿™ä¸€æˆ˜ç•¥ä¸¾æªä¸ä»…åŠ å‰§äº†ä¸ GaN-on-SiC çš„ç«äº‰ï¼Œè€Œä¸”è¿˜å¯èƒ½å¼€å¯æ–°çš„å‰æ™¯ï¼Œå°¤å…¶æ˜¯åœ¨æ‰‹æœºå¸‚åœºã€‚ 

æ ¹æ® Yoleé›†å›¢ã€Š  RF GaNå¤åˆåŠå¯¼ä½“ç›‘æµ‹ã€‹Q4-23ç‰ˆï¼Œåœ¨5Gç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½å’Œå›½é˜²é›·è¾¾åº”ç”¨éœ€æ±‚çš„æ¨åŠ¨ä¸‹ï¼ŒGaN RFå™¨ä»¶å¸‚åœºçš„æ•´ä½“ä»·å€¼é¢„è®¡å°†ä»14äº¿ç¾å…ƒé£™å‡è‡³22äº¿ç¾å…ƒä»¥ä¸Šï¼Œåœ¨2022-2028å¹´æœŸé—´å‘ˆç°å¼ºåŠ²çš„8.7%çš„å¤åˆå¹´å¢é•¿ç‡ï¼ˆCAGRï¼‰ã€‚ 

è™½ç„¶åœ¨ 2022-28 å¹´æœŸé—´ï¼ŒRF GaN å¸‚åœºçš„å‘å±•é€Ÿåº¦å¯èƒ½ä¸ä¼šä¸ç”¨äºåŠŸç‡è½¬æ¢åº”ç”¨çš„å®½å¸¦éš™ (SiC å’Œ GaN) å¸‚åœºå®Œå…¨ç›¸åŒï¼Œä½†å®ƒä»ç„¶å……æ»¡æ´»åŠ›å¹¶æ­£åœ¨æ”¹å˜å…¶ä¾›åº”é“¾ã€‚æ€»éƒ¨ä½äºç¾å›½çš„MACOMæ˜¯è¯¥è¡Œä¸šçš„ä¸»è¦å‚ä¸è€…ï¼Œå®ƒåœ¨ 2023 å¹´å®Œæˆäº†ä¸¤é¡¹é‡å¤§æ”¶è´­â€”â€”æ”¶è´­æ³•å›½OMMIC SASçš„ GaN-on-Si æŠ€æœ¯ï¼Œä»¥åŠæ”¶è´­ç¾å›½çš„Wolfspeed çš„RF GaN-on-SiC ä¸šåŠ¡ï¼Œåè€…æ˜¯ RF GaN é¢†åŸŸçš„é¢†å¯¼è€…ã€‚è¿™äº›æˆ˜ç•¥ä¸¾æªä½¿ MACOM æœ‰å¯èƒ½æˆä¸º RF GaN çš„é¢†å¯¼è€…ä¹‹ä¸€ã€‚åŒæ—¶ï¼ŒSEDIã€Qorvoå’ŒNXPç­‰å‚ä¸è€…åœ¨ RF GaN è¡Œä¸šä¿æŒç€å¼ºå¤§çš„é¢†å¯¼åœ°ä½ã€‚åœ¨ä¸­å›½ï¼ŒSICCã€ä¸‰å®‰é›†æˆç”µè·¯ã€Dynax å’Œ CETC ç­‰å…¬å¸ç»§ç»­å¼€å‘å’Œè§£å†³æœ¬åœ° RF GaN å¸‚åœºé—®é¢˜ã€‚æ—©åœ¨ 2023 å¹´ï¼Œè‹±é£å‡Œå°±å‘ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½å¸‚åœºæ¨å‡ºäº†é¦–ä¸ªåŸºäº 8 è‹±å¯¸æ™¶åœ†çš„å•†ç”¨ GaN-on-Si Pa æŠ€æœ¯ã€‚æ„æ³•åŠå¯¼ä½“ (ST Microelectronics)ã€è”åç”µå­ (UMC) å’Œæ ¼ç½—æ–¹å¾· (GlobalFoundries)ç­‰å…¶ä»–å…¬å¸ä¹Ÿå¯èƒ½åœ¨æœªæ¥å‡ å¹´æ•ˆä»¿ã€‚

**RF GaN åœ¨å¤šä¸ªåº”ç”¨é¢†åŸŸè·å¾—æˆåŠŸ**

![GaN](/picture/RF_GaN_1.jpeg)

è‡ª 20 ä¸–çºª 90 å¹´ä»£ä»¥æ¥ï¼Œç¾å›½å›½é˜²éƒ¨å·²ç»è®¤è¯†åˆ° RF GaN-on-SiC ç›¸æ¯” InPã€GaAs HBTã€GaAs HEMT å’Œ Si LDMOS ç­‰ææ–™å…·æœ‰æ›´å‡ºè‰²çš„è¾“å‡ºåŠŸç‡å’Œæ•ˆç‡ã€‚RF GaN ä¸ä»…æä¾›æ›´å®½çš„å¸¦å®½ï¼Œè€Œä¸”è¿˜æœ‰åŠ©äºå‡å°ç³»ç»Ÿå°ºå¯¸â€”â€”éšç€ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½æ‰©å±•å…¶é¢‘ç‡å’ŒåŸºç«™æ¨¡å‹ï¼Œè¿™ä¸¤ä¸ªå±æ€§å¤‡å—è¿½æ§ã€‚ 

RF GaN å…·æœ‰å‡ºè‰²çš„åŠŸç‡å’Œæ•ˆç‡ç‰¹æ€§ï¼Œå› æ­¤åœ¨å›½é˜²åº”ç”¨ä¸­å¾—åˆ°å¹¿æ³›é‡‡ç”¨ï¼Œç‰¹åˆ«æ˜¯åœ¨è§£å†³æœºè½½é›·è¾¾ç³»ç»Ÿç­‰é«˜åŠŸç‡åœºæ™¯ä¸­çš„çƒ­æŒ‘æˆ˜æ–¹é¢ã€‚å›½é˜²ç»§ç»­æˆä¸º RF GaN å¸‚åœºä¸­æœ€å¤§çš„é¢†åŸŸä¹‹ä¸€ã€‚ 

æœºè½½ç³»ç»Ÿçš„ç‰¹ç‚¹æ˜¯è®¾å¤‡æ•°é‡å¤šï¼Œé¢„è®¡å°†å æ®å¸‚åœºä¸»å¯¼åœ°ä½ï¼Œæœªæ¥å‡ å¹´ï¼Œèˆ°è½½ç³»ç»Ÿä¹Ÿæœ‰æœ›å¢é•¿ã€‚åœ¨ç¾å›½å¢ƒå¤–ï¼Œæ¬§æ´²å’Œä¸­å›½éƒ½åœ¨ç§¯æåŸ¹è‚²å…¶ GaN ç”Ÿæ€ç³»ç»Ÿï¼Œç‰¹åˆ«æ³¨é‡æ‰©å¤§åœ¨å†›ç”¨é›·è¾¾åº”ç”¨ä¸­çš„éƒ¨ç½²ã€‚å°½ç®¡ç”µå­æˆ˜å¸‚åœºåœ¨å¾ˆå¤§ç¨‹åº¦ä¸Šä»å¤„äºéšè”½å’Œä¿å¯†çŠ¶æ€ï¼Œä½†è¯¥é¢†åŸŸæ­£åœ¨è¿›è¡Œçš„æ¼”ç¤ºå’Œ GaN é¡¹ç›®ç¡®ä¿äº†æŒç»­å¢é•¿ã€‚ç”±äº GaN å…·æœ‰å®½å¸¦æ“ä½œå’Œå¢å¼ºçš„å¯é æ€§ï¼Œå› æ­¤æ¯”æ›¿ä»£æŠ€æœ¯æ›´å—ä¸šç•Œé’çã€‚é¢„è®¡åœ¨ 2022 å¹´è‡³ 2028 å¹´æœŸé—´ï¼Œå†›äº‹å«æ˜Ÿé€šä¿¡å°†å¤§å¹…å¢é•¿ã€‚GaN å™¨ä»¶æˆä¸ºéƒ¨ç½²Ka æ³¢æ®µå—ä¸Šå˜é¢‘å™¨ç³»ç»Ÿçš„é¦–é€‰ï¼Œå…·æœ‰é«˜åŠŸç‡è¾“å‡ºå’Œè½»é‡åŒ–ç‰¹æ€§ã€‚åœ¨Cå’ŒX æ³¢æ®µé¢†åŸŸï¼ŒGaN ç³»ç»Ÿçš„é€‰æ‹©ä»¥åŠŸç‡é™„åŠ æ•ˆç‡ (PAE) çš„å…³é”®æ ‡å‡†ä¸ºæŒ‡å¯¼ã€‚ 

ä¸æ­¤åŒæ—¶ï¼ŒRF GaN å·²å¼€å§‹è¿›å†›å«æ˜Ÿé€šä¿¡å¸‚åœºï¼Œåˆ©ç”¨å…¶ç›¸å¯¹äºå…¶ä»–ææ–™çš„é«˜æ•ˆç‡æ¥å®ç°æ›´å°çš„å™¨ä»¶å°ºå¯¸ï¼Œä»è€Œåœ¨ç³»ç»Ÿçº§èŠ‚çœå®è´µçš„ç©ºé—´ã€‚åœ¨ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½å’Œå›½é˜²å¸‚åœºä¹‹åï¼Œå«æ˜Ÿé€šä¿¡æ˜¯ç¬¬ä¸‰å¤§ RF GaN å¸‚åœºï¼Œé¢„è®¡åˆ° 2028 å¹´å°†è¾¾åˆ° 2.7 äº¿ç¾å…ƒï¼Œ2022-2028 å¹´å¤åˆå¹´å¢é•¿ç‡ä¸º 18% ã€‚RF GaN åŠŸç‡æ”¾å¤§å™¨æä¾›æ›´é«˜çš„æ•°æ®ååé‡ã€æ›´å°çš„å¤©çº¿ã€æ›´å®½çš„å¸¦å®½å’Œæ›´å¥½çš„æ•ˆç‡ã€‚ä» L/C/X æ³¢æ®µè¿‡æ¸¡åˆ°Ku / Ka æ³¢æ®µå¯å®ç°ç§»åŠ¨å«æ˜Ÿé€šä¿¡çš„æ›´é«˜æ•°æ®é€Ÿç‡ã€‚è™½ç„¶è¡Œæ³¢ç®¡ (TWT) æŠ€æœ¯åœ¨å†å²ä¸Šå æ®ä¸»å¯¼åœ°ä½ï¼Œä½†å®ƒå…·æœ‰ä½“ç§¯å¤§ã€å¯é æ€§é«˜ç­‰å±€é™æ€§ã€‚åŸºäº GaAs çš„å›ºæ€åŠŸç‡æ”¾å¤§å™¨ (SSPA) åœ¨ä½åŠŸè€—å’Œè½»é‡çº§å«æ˜Ÿç³»ç»Ÿä¸­è¶Šæ¥è¶Šå—åˆ°å…³æ³¨ï¼Œä½†ä¸ GaN ç›¸æ¯”ï¼Œå…¶æ•ˆç‡å’Œå¸¦å®½æœ‰é™ã€‚ GaN PA æ¯” GaAs SSPA å…·æœ‰è®¸å¤šä¼˜åŠ¿ï¼Œä½¿å…¶é€‚ç”¨äºå„ç§åº”ç”¨ï¼Œå¦‚ GEO HTSã€â€œæ–°ç©ºé—´â€ã€LEO å’Œæ›´é«˜é¢‘ç‡çš„åœ°çƒè§‚æµ‹ã€‚æˆ‘ä»¬çœ‹åˆ°äººä»¬å¯¹å«æ˜Ÿé€šä¿¡çš„å…³æ³¨åº¦æ—¥ç›Šå¢åŠ ï¼Œç‰¹åˆ«æ˜¯ç”±äºäººä»¬å¯¹â€œæ–°ç©ºé—´â€è¶‹åŠ¿çš„å…´è¶£æ—¥ç›Šæµ“åšã€‚æ­¤å¤–ï¼Œç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½è¡Œä¸šå¯¹å«æ˜Ÿé€šä¿¡çš„å…³æ³¨åº¦ä¹Ÿæ—¥ç›Šå¢åŠ ï¼Œå°¤å…¶æ˜¯ Space X è®¡åˆ’é€šè¿‡å«æ˜ŸæŠ€æœ¯æä¾› 5G è¦†ç›–ã€‚è¿™ç§æ–¹æ³•å¢åŠ äº†ä¸€ä¸ªæ²¡æœ‰ç¼ºä¹å¯é ç”µè¯ç½‘ç»œè¦†ç›–çš„åœ°åŒºçš„å¯èƒ½æ€§ã€‚RF GaN æŠ€æœ¯å¯ä»¥å€Ÿæ­¤æœºä¼šå¢åŠ å…¶åœ¨å¸‚åœºä¸Šçš„ä»½é¢ã€‚ 

æœ€åˆç”±åä¸ºäº 2015 å¹´æ¨å‡ºï¼Œç”¨äºç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½çš„ GaN-on-SiC äº 2020 å¹´å¼€å§‹æ‰¹é‡ç”Ÿäº§ï¼Œç”¨äº 4G åŸºç«™ã€‚ä»é‚£æ—¶èµ·ï¼ŒRF GaN æŠ€æœ¯å› æ»¡è¶³æ–°åŸºç«™è¦æ±‚å¹¶å–ä»£ LDMOS æŠ€æœ¯è€Œå—ç›Šäº 5G çš„æ¨å‡ºã€‚ä¸–ç•Œå„åœ°çš„å…¬å¸ä¹Ÿè¿›è¡Œäº†å¤§è§„æ¨¡æŠ•èµ„ï¼Œä¾‹å¦‚ SEDIã€Wolfspeedï¼ˆå…¶ RF ä¸šåŠ¡ç°å·²æˆä¸º MACOM çš„ä¸€éƒ¨åˆ†ï¼‰ã€NXP å’Œ Qorvoï¼Œç¡®ä¿ GaN-on-SiC åœ¨å…¶ç›®æ ‡åº”ç”¨ä¸­å æ®ä¸»å¯¼åœ°ä½å¹¶å–ä»£å…¶åŒç±» Si LDMOSã€‚ 

4Gå¾®ç«™å’Œå®ç«™ä¸»è¦åŸºäºè¿œç¨‹æ— çº¿ç”µå¤´ç«¯ï¼ˆRRHï¼‰ï¼Œé›†æˆäº†åŸºç«™çš„å°„é¢‘é“¾å’Œæ¨¡æ•°è½¬æ¢ç»„ä»¶ä»¥åŠæœ€å¤šå…«ä¸ªå¤šæµPAï¼Œè¾“å‡ºåŠŸç‡é«˜è¾¾100Wã€‚ 

éšç€ 4G æ—¶ä»£çš„ç»“æŸï¼Œ3GHz åŸºç«™å¯¹åŸºäº LDMOS çš„ PA çš„ä¾èµ–é¢„è®¡å°†é€æ¸å‡å°‘ã€‚æ–°å…´çš„6GHz ä»¥ä¸‹ 5GåŸºç«™æ­£åœ¨ä» 2x2 MIMO æ¨¡å‹è½¬å˜ä¸º 64x64å¤§è§„æ¨¡ MIMO (mMIMO)ï¼Œå…¶ä¸­æœ‰æºå¤©çº¿ç³»ç»Ÿ (AAS) å–ä»£äº† RRHã€‚ 

åœ¨å¢åŠ  PA æ•°é‡çš„åŒæ—¶ï¼Œæ¯ä¸ª PA çš„è¾“å‡ºåŠŸç‡æœ‰æœ›é™ä½ï¼ˆä» 100W é™è‡³ 5Wï¼‰ï¼ŒåŒæ—¶è¿˜è¦æ±‚ PA èƒ½å¤Ÿå¤„ç†ä¸æ–­å¢åŠ çš„æ•°æ®æµé‡ï¼ŒåŒæ—¶é™ä½åŠŸè€—ã€‚ 

GaN å¯ä»¥æ»¡è¶³æ‰€æœ‰è¿™äº›è¦æ±‚ã€‚ç”±äº GaN-on-SiC å¯æ»¡è¶³ 5G é«˜è¾¾ 7GHz çš„é¢‘ç‡ï¼ŒLDMOS çš„å¸‚åœºä»½é¢é¢„è®¡å°†ä¸‹é™ã€‚å¯¹äº5G mmWaveå’Œ6Gï¼Œç”±äºå¯¹é«˜é¢‘å’Œä½åŠŸè€—çš„è¦æ±‚æ›´é«˜ï¼ŒRF GaN æŠ€æœ¯é¢„è®¡å°†é¢ä¸´æ¥è‡ª SiGe å’Œ InP æŠ€æœ¯ç­‰å…¶ä»–ææ–™çš„æ›´æ¿€çƒˆç«äº‰ã€‚ 

**RF GaNå°†å¦‚ä½•å‘å±•ï¼Ÿ**

ç”±äº 6GHz ä»¥ä¸‹çš„ 5G ç”µä¿¡åŸºç«™éœ€è¦åŠŸç‡æ›´ä½çš„ PAï¼Œå› æ­¤ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“æœ‰æœ›åœ¨ 10W ä»¥ä¸‹çš„ 32T32R / 64T64R mMIMO åŸºç«™ä¸­å æ®ä¸€å¸­ä¹‹åœ°ã€‚åœ¨è¿‡å»ä¸¤å¹´ä¸­ï¼Œæ„æ³•åŠå¯¼ä½“ (STMicroelectronics)ã€MACOMã€OMMICï¼ˆç°ä¸º MACOM çš„ä¸€éƒ¨åˆ†ï¼‰ã€GCSã€è‹±é£å‡Œç§‘æŠ€ç­‰ä¸»è¦å‚ä¸è€…ä»¥åŠæ ¼èŠ¯å’Œè”åç”µå­ç­‰ä»£å·¥å‚åˆä½œæ¨å‡ºäº† RF ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“æŠ€æœ¯ã€‚ 

å‘åœ¨ 28 â€“ 60GHz ä¸‹å·¥ä½œä¸”è¾“å‡ºåŠŸç‡é™ä½çš„æ¯«ç±³æ³¢å°å‹èœ‚çªï¼ˆ2 æµå’Œ 4 æµï¼‰çš„è½¬å˜ä¸ºç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“æä¾›äº†é¢å¤–çš„æœºä¼šã€‚éšç€ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½è¶Šæ¥è¶Šå¤šåœ°é‡‡ç”¨è¾ƒä½è¾“å‡ºåŠŸç‡ç³»ç»Ÿï¼Œå¤©çº¿é˜µåˆ—ç³»ç»Ÿ (AAS) å’Œå°å‹èœ‚çªçš„éœ€æ±‚æ¨åŠ¨äº†ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„é‡‡ç”¨ï¼Œä»¥æ»¡è¶³å¤šæµã€å°å‹èœ‚çªå’Œæ¯«ç±³æ³¢æ³¢æŸå½¢æˆå™¨æ€§èƒ½çš„éœ€æ±‚ã€‚å±•æœ›ä¸‹ä¸€ä»£ 6Gï¼Œå…¶é¢‘ç‡å°†æ›´é«˜ï¼Œé¢„è®¡ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“å°†ä¸ç°æœ‰æŠ€æœ¯ç¢³åŒ–ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“å…±å­˜ã€‚

![GaN](/picture/RF_GaN_2.jpeg)

ä»Šå¹´ï¼Œè‹±é£å‡Œç§‘æŠ€å…¬å¸å–å¾—äº†é‡å¤§è¿›å±•ï¼Œæ¨å‡ºäº†åŸºäº 8 è‹±å¯¸æŠ€æœ¯çš„ GaN-on-Si PAï¼Œä»¥æ»¡è¶³ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½å¸‚åœºçš„éœ€æ±‚ã€‚é¢„è§åˆ°è¿™ä¸€è¶‹åŠ¿ï¼ŒGlobal Foundriesã€UMCã€MACOM å’Œ STMicroelectronics ç­‰å…¶ä»–ä¸»è¦å‚ä¸è€…é¢„è®¡å°†åœ¨æœªæ¥å‡ å¹´æ•ˆä»¿ã€‚å€¼å¾—æ³¨æ„çš„æ˜¯ï¼Œè®¸å¤šå‚ä¸è€…é€‰æ‹©ç›´æ¥ä½¿ç”¨ GaN-on-Si è¿›å…¥å¸‚åœºï¼Œè€Œä¸ç”¨ GaN-on-SiC æŠ€æœ¯ã€‚ 

é¢„è®¡åˆ° 2028 å¹´ï¼ŒGaN å°†å ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½ PA è®¾å¤‡å‡ºè´§é‡çš„ 87% ä»¥ä¸Šã€‚å…¶ä¸­ï¼Œè¶…è¿‡ 77% å°†æ˜¯ SiC ä¸Š GaNï¼Œ10% å°†æ˜¯ç¡…ä¸Š GaNï¼Œè€Œ LDMOS é¢„è®¡å°†å¤±å»å¸‚åœºä»½é¢ã€‚

![GaN](/picture/RF_GaN_3.jpeg)

GaN-on-Si æŠ€æœ¯çš„å‰æ™¯å»¶ä¼¸è‡³ FR3 é¢‘æ®µçš„ 5G æ‰‹æœºåŠŸç‡æ”¾å¤§å™¨ã€‚è™½ç„¶ GaN-on-Si åœ¨æ‰‹æœºåŠŸç‡æ”¾å¤§å™¨çš„ 7GHz ä»¥ä¸‹å’Œ 5G æ¯«ç±³æ³¢é¢‘ç‡æ–¹é¢å…·æœ‰æ½œåŠ›ï¼Œä½†å¿…é¡»æ‰¿è®¤æˆç†Ÿçš„ GaAs è§£å†³æ–¹æ¡ˆåœ¨ 7GHz ä»¥ä¸‹çš„ç°æœ‰ä¸»å¯¼åœ°ä½ä»¥åŠç¡…åŸºè§£å†³æ–¹æ¡ˆåœ¨æ¯«ç±³æ³¢åº”ç”¨ä¸­çš„å¸å¼•åŠ›ã€‚è¿™äº›æŠ€æœ¯åœ¨æŠ€æœ¯å’Œä¾›åº”é“¾æ–¹é¢éƒ½å·²æˆç†Ÿï¼Œæ˜¯é‡è¦çš„ç«äº‰å¯¹æ‰‹ã€‚åœ¨ FR3 çš„å…¬å¼€ç«äº‰ä¸­ï¼ŒGaN-on-Si å¾ˆæœ‰å‰æ™¯ï¼Œä½†éœ€è¦è¿›è¡Œå¤æ‚çš„è®¾è®¡æ›´æ”¹æ‰èƒ½é›†æˆåˆ°æ‰‹æœºç³»ç»Ÿä¸­ï¼Œå› æ­¤å°†å…¶åº”ç”¨äº FR3 é¢‘æ®µæ˜¯ä¸€ä¸ªé•¿æœŸç›®æ ‡ã€‚ 

GaN-on-SiæŠ€æœ¯å‘½è¿çš„å†³å®šæ€§å½±å“æœ€ç»ˆåœ¨äºè‹¹æœã€ä¸‰æ˜Ÿã€å°ç±³ç­‰æ™ºèƒ½æ‰‹æœºOEMï¼Œè¿™å¯èƒ½æˆä¸ºGaN-on-Siè¡Œä¸šçš„è½¬æŠ˜ç‚¹ã€‚

å¦‚ä»Šï¼Œä½œä¸ºä¸»è¦å¹³å°çš„ GaN-on-SiC æ‹¥æœ‰å®Œå–„çš„ä¾›åº”é“¾ã€‚SEDIã€Qorvoã€Wolfspeed å’Œ NXP ç­‰è®¾å¤‡ä¾›åº”å•†ä»¥åŠå›½é˜²ç›¸å…³å…¬å¸Raytheonã€BAE Systemså’ŒNorthrop Grummanéƒ½æä¾› GaN-on-SiC æŠ€æœ¯ã€‚2022 å¹´ï¼ŒSEDIã€Qorvo å’Œ Wolfspeed æ˜¯ RF GaN é¢†åŸŸçš„é¢†å…ˆä¼ä¸šã€‚ä½œä¸º GaN é¢†åŸŸçš„æ–°äººï¼ŒNXP äº 2020 å¹´åœ¨ç¾å›½å¼€è®¾äº† 6 è‹±å¯¸ GaN-on-SiC æ™¶åœ†å‚ï¼Œè¿›å…¥ç”µä¿¡ä¾›åº”é“¾ï¼Œå®ç°äº†æ˜¾ç€å¢é•¿ã€‚åœ¨çŸ­æ—¶é—´å†…ï¼Œè¯¥å…¬å¸è¿˜æ‹¥æœ‰ LDMOS äº§å“ï¼Œå·²æˆä¸ºåŸºäº GaN çš„ç”µä¿¡åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½é¢†åŸŸçš„é¢†å…ˆä¼ä¸šã€‚æ­¤å¤–ï¼Œåœ¨è¿‡å»å‡ å¹´ä¸­ï¼ŒGaN-on-SiC è¿˜è¿æ¥äº† Altum RFã€mmTron å’Œ Gallium semiconductors ç­‰åˆ›æ–°ä¼ä¸šçš„åŠ å…¥ã€‚ç°åœ¨ï¼Œè¿™ä¸ªä¸æ–­æ‰©å¼ çš„è¡Œä¸šä¸º GaN-on-Si æŠ€æœ¯æä¾›äº†æ›´å¤§çš„ç©ºé—´ï¼Œå…¶ä¸­ä½åŠŸè€— GaN è§£å†³æ–¹æ¡ˆæœ‰æœ›ç”¨äºä½äº 10W çš„ 32T32R / 64T64R mMIMO åŸºç«™ï¼Œå¹¶ä¸”ä»Šå¹´å°†æœ‰è¶Šæ¥è¶Šå¤šçš„äº§å“ä¸Šå¸‚ã€‚ 

SI SiC æ™¶åœ†å¸‚åœºä»ç”±ä¸‰å¤§ä¾›åº”å•† Wolfspeedã€Coherent å’Œ SICC å æ®ã€‚åœ¨å›½é˜²é¢†åŸŸï¼Œé›·ç¥å…¬å¸ã€è¯ºæ–¯ç½—æ™®Â·æ ¼é²æ›¼å…¬å¸å’Œä¸­å›½ç”µå­ç§‘æŠ€é›†å›¢åœ¨ GaN çš„åº”ç”¨æ–¹é¢å¤„äºé¢†å…ˆåœ°ä½ã€‚å›½é˜²éƒ¨ä¿¡ä»»çš„ Wolfspeed å’Œ Qorvo ä¹Ÿæ˜¯ GaN ä»£å·¥å‚ã€‚çˆ±ç«‹ä¿¡å’Œè¯ºåŸºäºšä¸“æ³¨äºç”µä¿¡å¸‚åœºçš„ä¾›åº”ï¼Œä¸æ–­æ‰©å¤§æ¥è‡ªå¤šå®¶è®¾å¤‡ä¾›åº”å•†çš„ RF GaN è®¾å¤‡ä¾›åº”é‡ï¼Œè€Œä¸‰æ˜Ÿåˆ™ä¸éŸ©å›½è®¾å¤‡åˆ¶é€ å•†å¯†åˆ‡åˆä½œã€‚è‡ªç¾å›½åˆ¶è£ä»¥æ¥ï¼Œåä¸ºå’Œä¸­å…´é€šè®¯å·²è½¬å‘ä¸­å›½ä¾›åº”é“¾ä»¥å‘å±•å›½å†…äº§èƒ½ã€‚ 

ä¸ºäº†å…‹æœç¾å›½çš„åˆ¶è£ï¼Œä¸­å›½ç»§ç»­å‘å±•å›½å†…çš„å°„é¢‘ GaN æŠ€æœ¯å’Œä¸­å›½ä¾›åº”é“¾ã€‚åœ¨ GaN-on-SiC ç”Ÿæ€ç³»ç»Ÿä¸­ï¼Œé¢†å…ˆçš„å‚ä¸è€…åœ¨æ™¶åœ†å’Œç»ˆç«¯ç³»ç»Ÿå±‚é¢éƒ½æ˜¯ä¸–ç•Œä¸€æµçš„ï¼Œä¾‹å¦‚ SICCã€ä¸‰å®‰é›†æˆç”µè·¯ã€CETCã€Dynaxã€åä¸ºå’Œä¸­å…´é€šè®¯ã€‚è‡ª 2020 å¹´ä»¥æ¥ï¼Œä¸­å›½ä¸€ç›´åœ¨åŠ é€Ÿå¤–å»¶ç‰‡ã€å‰ç«¯å’Œåç«¯å·¥è‰ºå’Œè®¾è®¡çš„å¼€å‘ã€‚æ¯ä¸ªçº§åˆ«éƒ½ç¡®å®šäº†ä¸æ­¢ä¸€ä¸ªæ´»è·ƒçš„å‚ä¸è€…ï¼Œå±•ç¤ºäº†ä¸­å›½ç”Ÿæ€ç³»ç»Ÿåœ¨è¿‡å»ä¸¤å¹´ä¸­çš„è¿›æ­¥ã€‚åœ¨å™¨ä»¶å±‚é¢ï¼Œæµ·å¨åå’Œä¸‰å®‰é›†æˆç”µè·¯å·²ç»æä¾› 0.25Âµm èŠ‚ç‚¹çš„ GaN-on-SiCï¼Œä»¥æœåŠ¡äºç°æœ‰çš„ 6GHz ä»¥ä¸‹å¸‚åœºã€‚æ®æˆ‘ä»¬äº†è§£ï¼Œä¸‰å®‰é›†æˆç”µè·¯ä¹Ÿåœ¨åŠªåŠ›å¼€å‘ GaN-on-Si æŠ€æœ¯ã€‚

# 12.FR3 é¢‘ç‡èŒƒå›´

åœ¨æ¬§ç¾æ°®åŒ–é•“ä»£å·¥æ–¹é¢ï¼Œåˆ™æœ‰UMSå…¬å¸å’ŒOMMICå…¬å¸ã€‚å…¶ä¸­ï¼Œ<font color=red>UMSæ˜¯æ³•å›½ä¸€å®¶åŠå¯¼ä½“å…¬å¸ï¼Œä¸»è¦é’ˆå¯¹å°„é¢‘å™¨ä»¶æµç‰‡æä¾›æ°®åŒ–é•“å’Œç ·åŒ–é•“çš„ä»£å·¥æœåŠ¡</font>ã€‚UMSä»£å·¥çš„äº§å“ä¸»è¦é¢å‘å›½é˜²ï¼Œèˆªå¤©ç­‰å¸‚åœºï¼Œå…¶å·¥è‰ºå·²ç»è·å¾—æ¬§æ´²èˆªå¤©éƒ¨çš„è®¤è¯ã€‚å¦å¤–ï¼Œ<font color=red>OMMICæ­¤å‰ä¹Ÿä¸“æ³¨äºå¤ªç©ºå¸‚åœºï¼Œä¸»è¦è‡´åŠ›äºç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“æŠ€æœ¯</font>ï¼Œ2019å¹´OMMICæ¨å‡ºäº†ä¸€ç§æ–°çš„100çº³ç±³æ …æé•¿åº¦çš„<font color=blue>ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“å·¥è‰ºï¼Œç”¨äºå°„é¢‘åŠŸç‡å’Œä½å™ªå£°ï¼Œå…¶ç›®æ ‡æ˜¯5GåŸºç«™å’Œæ±½è½¦åº”ç”¨</font>ï¼ŒåŒæ—¶ï¼Œå…¬å¸ä¹Ÿå®£å¸ƒè®¡åˆ’OMMICæœ€ç»ˆä¼šå°†äº§é‡æé«˜åˆ°æ¯å¹´200å¤šä¸‡ç‰‡ï¼Œä»¥è§£å†³é‡äº§å¸‚åœºçš„éœ€æ±‚ã€‚

å¤§é™†æ–¹é¢çš„æ–°å…´ä»£å·¥å‚ä¸­ï¼Œ<font color=red>ä¸‰å®‰é›†æˆå’Œæµ·å¨åèŠ¯å…·æœ‰é‡äº§GaNåŠŸç‡å™¨ä»¶çš„èƒ½åŠ›</font>ã€‚å…¶ä¸­ï¼Œä¸‰å®‰é›†æˆæ˜¯LEDèŠ¯ç‰‡åˆ¶é€ å…¬å¸ä¸‰å®‰å…‰ç”µä¸‹å±å­å…¬å¸ï¼Œä¸»è¥æ°®åŒ–é•“å’Œç ·åŒ–é•“æŠ€æœ¯ç›¸å…³ä¸šåŠ¡ï¼Œæ˜¯ä¸€å®¶ä¸“é—¨ä»äº‹åŒ–åˆç‰©åŠå¯¼ä½“åˆ¶é€ çš„ä»£å·¥å‚ã€‚æ­¤å¤–ï¼Œæµ·å¨åèŠ¯æ˜¯å›½å†…é¦–å®¶æä¾›6å‹ç ·åŒ–é•“/æ°®åŒ–é•“å¾®æ³¢é›†æˆç”µï¼ˆGaAs/GaN MMICï¼‰çš„çº¯æ™¶åœ†ä»£å·¥æœåŠ¡çš„åˆ¶é€ ä¼ä¸šï¼Œäº§å“ä¸»è¦é¢å‘5Gã€é›·è¾¾ ã€æ–°èƒ½æºã€ç‰©è”ç½‘ç­‰é«˜ç«¯èŠ¯ç‰‡å¸‚åœºã€‚æ®æ‚‰ï¼Œå…¬å¸çš„æ°®åŒ–é•“å·²æˆåŠŸçªç ´6å‹æ°®åŒ–é•“æ™¶åœ†é”®åˆæŠ€æœ¯ã€‚åœ¨äº§èƒ½æ–¹é¢ï¼Œç›®å‰ï¼Œæµ·å¨åèŠ¯æ°®åŒ–é•“è§„åˆ’äº§èƒ½600ç‰‡/æœˆã€‚

## 14.2 GlobalFoundries

ä¸æ­¤åŒæ—¶ï¼ŒåŠ å·¥åçš„SiCæ™¶åœ†ä¾›åº”ä¸ç”µåŠ›ç”µå­å¸‚åœºçš„éœ€æ±‚ä¿æŒç€å¯†åˆ‡è”ç³»ï¼ˆå¸‚åœºæ•°æ®ï¼šåŠŸç‡SiCï¼‰ï¼Œéšç€è¡Œä¸šå‘8è‹±å¯¸æ™¶åœ†ç›´å¾„è¿‡æ¸¡ï¼Œåˆ°2024å¹´ï¼Œå…¶äº§é‡å°†è¾¾åˆ°çº¦230ä¸‡ç‰‡6è‹±å¯¸å½“é‡æ™¶åœ†ã€‚åœ¨è®¾å¤‡å‡çº§å’Œæ–°ç”Ÿäº§çº¿çš„æ”¯æŒä¸‹ï¼Œå‘æ›´å¤§æ™¶åœ†çš„è½¬å˜æé«˜äº†æ™¶åœ†çš„å‡åŒ€æ€§ï¼Œé™ä½äº†ç¼ºé™·ç‡ï¼Œå¹¶æå‡äº†æ•´ä½“ç”Ÿäº§ç‡ã€‚

ç„¶è€Œï¼Œéšç€ç”µåŠ¨æ±½è½¦å¸‚åœºå¢é•¿æ”¾ç¼“ï¼ŒSiCæ™¶åœ†åˆ¶é€ æ‰©å¼ çš„æ­¥ä¼ä¹Ÿåœ¨æ”¾ç¼“ã€‚ä¸€äº›å…¬å¸æ­£åœ¨ç¼©å‡å…¶äº§èƒ½æ‰©å¼ è®¡åˆ’ï¼›ä¾‹å¦‚ï¼ŒWolfspeed æ­£åœ¨å…³é—­å…¶ä½äºè¾¾å‹’å§†çš„ 6 è‹±å¯¸æ™¶åœ†å‚ï¼Œè‹±é£å‡Œæ­£åœ¨æ¨è¿Ÿå…¶å±…æ—æ‰©å»ºçš„ç¬¬äºŒé˜¶æ®µï¼Œå®‰æ£®ç¾åŠå¯¼ä½“åˆ™æš‚åœäº†å¯¹å…¶å¯Œå·å·¥å‚çš„æŠ•èµ„ã€‚è¿™ç§å‡é€Ÿæ­£åœ¨æŠµæ¶ˆæ­¤å‰ç”±å»å…¨çƒåŒ–æ¨åŠ¨çš„åŠ¿å¤´ï¼Œè€Œå»å…¨çƒåŒ–æ›¾æ˜¯äº§èƒ½å¢é•¿çš„ä¸»è¦é©±åŠ¨åŠ›ã€‚

é¢„è®¡é‡ç‚¹å°†ä»ç§¯æçš„äº§èƒ½å»ºè®¾è½¬å‘ä¼˜åŒ–ç°æœ‰èµ„äº§å’Œæé«˜äº§é‡ï¼Œå°¤å…¶æ˜¯åœ¨ 8 è‹±å¯¸ç”Ÿäº§çº¿ä¸Šã€‚ä¸­æœŸå‰æ™¯å¯èƒ½ä»¥è°¨æ…å’Œé‡æ–°è¯„ä¼°æ‰©å¼ è®¡åˆ’ä¸ºç‰¹å¾ã€‚ç›‘æµ‹ç”µåŠ¨æ±½è½¦ã€å·¥ä¸šå’Œå¯å†ç”Ÿèƒ½æºåº”ç”¨ä¸­å¯¹ SiC çš„ç»“æ„æ€§éœ€æ±‚å°†æ˜¯å…³é”®ï¼Œå°¤å…¶æ˜¯åœ¨å»å…¨çƒåŒ–å’Œå¼¹æ€§ä¾›åº”é“¾å»ºè®¾çš„èƒŒæ™¯ä¸‹ã€‚å›¾ 1 æ¦‚è¿°äº†å…¨çƒç°æœ‰å’Œè®¡åˆ’ä¸­çš„åŠå¯¼ä½“åˆ¶é€ ç”Ÿäº§çº¿çš„å·²å®‰è£…å’Œé¢„æœŸ SiC æ™¶åœ†äº§èƒ½ã€‚è¯¥å›¾è¡¨è¡¨ç¤ºå·¥å‚ä½ç½®ã€‚æ€»ä½“è€Œè¨€ï¼Œé¢„è®¡ 6 è‹±å¯¸æ™¶åœ†çš„äº§é‡å°†ç¨³å®šåœ¨æ¯æœˆ 350,000 ç‰‡å·¦å³ã€‚åˆ° 2029 å¹´ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬é¢„è®¡ 8 è‹±å¯¸ SiC èŠ¯ç‰‡çš„äº§é‡å°†ä¸ç›®å‰çš„ 6 è‹±å¯¸æ™¶åœ†äº§é‡ç›¸åŒ¹é…ã€‚ç›®å‰ï¼Œä¸­å›½å å…¨çƒ SiC äº§èƒ½çš„ 30%ï¼Œå…¶æ¬¡æ˜¯æ¬§æ´²ï¼ˆ21%ï¼‰ã€ç¾å›½ï¼ˆ14%ï¼‰ã€æ—¥æœ¬ï¼ˆ14%ï¼‰å’ŒéŸ©å›½ï¼ˆ12%ï¼‰ã€‚å°æ¹¾å’Œå…¶ä»–äºšæ´²å›½å®¶/åœ°åŒºå æ®å‰©ä½™äº§èƒ½ã€‚äº§èƒ½æ‰©å¼ çš„æ¼”å˜å¾ˆå¤§ç¨‹åº¦ä¸Šå–å†³äºå¸‚åœºå‘å±•å’Œå…³ç¨çš„å½±å“ã€‚æœ‰æ‰©å¼ è®¡åˆ’çš„åŠŸç‡åŠå¯¼ä½“å…¬å¸å¯èƒ½ä¼šç­‰å¾…å³å°†å‡ºå°çš„æ–°è´¸æ˜“è§„åˆ™æ˜ç¡®åï¼Œç›¸åº”åœ°è°ƒæ•´å…¶åˆ¶é€ å¸ƒå±€æˆ˜ç•¥ã€‚ä¸æ­¤åŒæ—¶ï¼Œå»ºç«‹å·¥å‚æˆ–ç”Ÿäº§çº¿éœ€è¦24è‡³36ä¸ªæœˆçš„æ—¶é—´ï¼Œä»å»ºç­‘æ–½å·¥åˆ°å·¥å…·å®‰è£…å’Œè®¤è¯ï¼Œéœ€è¦ç²¾å¿ƒè§„åˆ’ã€‚

è¿™äº›æ”¹è¿›ç°åœ¨ä½¿ 8 è‹±å¯¸æ™¶åœ†çš„äº§èƒ½æ‰©å¼ æˆä¸ºå¯èƒ½ï¼Œå¹¶ä¸ºå‘ 12 è‹±å¯¸è¿‡æ¸¡å¥ å®šäº†åŸºç¡€ã€‚ä¾‹å¦‚ï¼ŒInnoscience å·²åœ¨ 8 è‹±å¯¸æ™¶åœ†ä¸Šé‡äº§å¢å¼ºå‹ GaNï¼›è‹±é£å‡Œå·²ç»è¯æ˜äº† 12 è‹±å¯¸è§„æ¨¡ GaN çš„å¯è¡Œæ€§ï¼›å¾·å·ä»ªå™¨è®¡åˆ’é€šè¿‡åœ¨å…¶ä¼šæ´¥æ™¶åœ†å‚æé«˜ 8 è‹±å¯¸äº§é‡ï¼ˆå®Œå…¨è½¬ç§»åˆ° 12 è‹±å¯¸ï¼‰æ¥å°†å…¶ GaN äº§é‡ç¿»ä¸¤ç•ªã€‚è¿™äº›ä¸¾æªæ—¨åœ¨ä¸º GaN çš„ä¸‹ä¸€æ³¢å¢é•¿åšå¥½å‡†å¤‡ï¼Œæ­£å¦‚æˆ‘ä»¬åœ¨ã€Š2025 å¹´åŠŸç‡åŠå¯¼ä½“çš„äº”å¤§å…³é”®è¶‹åŠ¿ã€‹ä¸­æ‰€è®¨è®ºçš„é‚£æ ·ã€‚å›¾ 2 æ¦‚è¿°äº†å…¨çƒç°æœ‰å’Œè®¡åˆ’ä¸­çš„åŠå¯¼ä½“ç”Ÿäº§çº¿çš„å·²å®‰è£…å’Œé¢„æœŸ GaN æ™¶åœ†äº§èƒ½ã€‚8 è‹±å¯¸æ™¶åœ†å·²ç»æˆä¸ºä¸»æµåŸºæ¿ï¼Œä¸­å›½åœ¨è¯¥é¢†åŸŸçš„ä¸»å¯¼åœ°ä½ç”šè‡³æ¯”åœ¨ SiC ç”Ÿäº§æ–¹é¢æ›´ä¸ºæ˜æ˜¾ã€‚è™½ç„¶12è‹±å¯¸GaNæŠ€æœ¯å°šå¤„äºå‘å±•åˆæœŸï¼Œä½†æˆ‘ä»¬é¢„è®¡åˆ°2028å¹´å®ƒå°†å åˆ°å…¨çƒæ€»äº§é‡çš„10%ã€‚2024å¹´ï¼Œä¸­å›½å¤§é™†çš„GaNæ™¶åœ†åˆ¶é€ äº§èƒ½å°†å å…¨çƒäº§èƒ½çš„57%ï¼Œå…¶æ¬¡æ˜¯å°æ¹¾åœ°åŒºï¼ˆ14%ï¼‰ã€æ—¥æœ¬ï¼ˆ11%ï¼‰ã€æ¬§æ´²ï¼ˆ10%ï¼‰å’Œç¾å›½ï¼ˆ4%ï¼‰ã€‚8è‹±å¯¸äº§èƒ½çš„åºå¤§æˆ–è®¸æ˜¯ä¸­å›½é¢†å…ˆçš„GaNåˆ¶é€ å•†è‹±è¯ºèµ›å…‹ï¼ˆInnoscienceï¼‰åœ¨åŠŸç‡GaNå¸‚åœºå æ®ä¸»å¯¼åœ°ä½çš„åŸå› ä¹‹ä¸€ã€‚ä¾‹å¦‚ï¼ŒTechInsightsåœ¨æ„æ³•åŠå¯¼ä½“ï¼ˆSTMicroelectronicsï¼‰çš„VIPerGaN65Dé«˜å‹è½¬æ¢å™¨ä¸Šå‘ç°äº†è‹±è¯ºèµ›å…‹çš„GaNèŠ¯ç‰‡ã€‚

ä»æ”¶å…¥è§’åº¦æ¥çœ‹ï¼Œæƒ…å†µæ­£å¥½ç›¸åã€‚æ ¹æ®æˆ‘ä»¬çš„åŠŸç‡åŠå¯¼ä½“å¸‚åœºä»½é¢æ•°æ®ï¼Œä¸­å›½ä¼ä¸šåœ¨åŠŸç‡åŠå¯¼ä½“å¸‚åœºï¼ˆåŒ…æ‹¬å®½å¸¦éš™æŠ€æœ¯ï¼‰ä¸­ä»ç„¶åªå è¾ƒå°ä»½é¢ï¼Œä»…æ¬¡äºæ¬§æ´²ã€åŒ—ç¾å’Œæ—¥æœ¬ä¼ä¸šã€‚ç„¶è€Œï¼Œä»–ä»¬çš„ä»½é¢æ­£åœ¨ç¨³æ­¥å¢é•¿ï¼Œå¹¶åœ¨ä¾›åº”é“¾ä¸­å æ®ä¸»å¯¼åœ°ä½ï¼Œå¹¶è·å¾—äº†é¢‡å…·æŒ‘æˆ˜æ€§çš„æ±½è½¦çº§è®¤è¯ã€‚

## 14.4 TSMC

### 14.4.1 å°ç§¯ç”µè®¡åˆ’é€€å‡ºï¼ŒNavitas å°† GaN ç”Ÿäº§è½¬ç§»è‡³ PSMC

çº³å¾®åŠå¯¼ä½“ (Navitas Semiconductor) å®£å¸ƒä¸å°æ¹¾æ™¶åœ†ä»£å·¥å‚åŠ›æ™¶åŠå¯¼ä½“åˆ¶é€ è‚¡ä»½æœ‰é™å…¬å¸ (PSMC) å»ºç«‹æˆ˜ç•¥åˆä½œä¼™ä¼´å…³ç³»ï¼Œå¯åŠ¨ 200 æ¯«ç±³ç¡…åŸºæ°®åŒ–é•“ (GaN-on-silicon) æŠ€æœ¯çš„ç”Ÿäº§å¹¶æ¨è¿›å…¶å¼€å‘ã€‚

æ ¹æ®æ­¤æ¬¡åˆä½œï¼Œçº³å¾®çš„GaN ICäº§å“ç»„åˆå°†åœ¨åŠ›æ™¶ä½äºç«¹å—ç§‘æŠ€å›­åŒºçš„æ™¶åœ†å‚8Bå‚ç”Ÿäº§ï¼Œé‡‡ç”¨åŠ›æ™¶180çº³ç±³åˆ†ç«‹å¼å·¥è‰ºæµç¨‹ã€‚åŠ›æ™¶æ­£åœ¨ç§¯æå¼€å‘è¯¥èŠ‚ç‚¹çš„100Vã€200Vå’Œ650V GaNå¹³å°ï¼ŒåŠ›äº‰æˆä¸ºä¸æ–­å‘å±•çš„GaNä¾›åº”é“¾ä¸­çš„å…³é”®å‚ä¸è€…ã€‚

æœ¬æ–‡å±•ç¤ºäº†åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„è°æŒ¯éš§ç©¿äºŒæç®¡ (RTD) æŒ¯è¡å™¨ï¼Œè¯¥æŒ¯è¡å™¨é‡‡ç”¨å•ç‰‡å¾®æ³¢é›†æˆç”µè·¯ã€‚é‡‡ç”¨é‡‘å±æœ‰æœºåŒ–å­¦æ°”ç›¸æ²‰ç§¯æ³•åœ¨è‡ªç”±æ‚¬æµ®çš„ c é¢åŠç»ç¼˜æ°®åŒ–é•“è¡¬åº•ä¸Šç”Ÿé•¿äº†å…·æœ‰æ°®åŒ–é•“é‡å­é˜±å’Œæ°®åŒ–é“åŒåŠ¿å’çš„åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTDã€‚ç”µè·¯å…ƒä»¶ï¼ŒåŒ…æ‹¬ RTDã€å…±é¢æ³¢å¯¼ã€é‡‘å±-ç»ç¼˜ä½“-é‡‘å±ç”µå®¹å™¨å’Œåˆ†æµç”µé˜»ï¼Œåœ¨æ°®åŒ–é•“è¡¬åº•ä¸Šå•ç‰‡é›†æˆã€‚ç”µè·¯åœ¨åŸºé¢‘ä¸º 17 GHz æ—¶æŒ¯è¡ï¼Œè¿™ä¸ä½¿ç”¨ä¸‰ç»´ç”µç£æ¨¡æ‹Ÿå™¨å’Œç”µè·¯æ¨¡æ‹Ÿå™¨ä¼°ç®—çš„é¢‘ç‡éå¸¸æ¥è¿‘ã€‚è¿™é¡¹ç ”ç©¶ä¿ƒè¿›äº†åŠå¯¼ä½“é«˜é¢‘å™¨ä»¶åœ¨æ¯«ç±³æ³¢å’Œå¤ªèµ«å…¹åº”ç”¨ä¸­çš„å‘å±•ã€‚

è°æŒ¯éš§ç©¿äºŒæç®¡ (RTD) èƒ½å¤Ÿå®ç°é«˜é¢‘å’Œé«˜åŠŸç‡æŒ¯è¡å™¨ï¼Œæ˜¯æ¯«ç±³æ³¢å’Œå¤ªèµ«å…¹å…‰æºçš„å¼ºæœ‰åŠ›å€™é€‰è€…ã€‚RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨ä¸»è¦é‡‡ç”¨ III æ—ç ·åŒ–ç‰©ã€ç£·åŒ–ç‰©å’Œé”‘åŒ–ç‰©ææ–™è¿›è¡Œç ”ç©¶ã€‚InGaAs/AlAs RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨åœ¨åŸºé¢‘æ–¹é¢å·²è¾¾åˆ°çº¦ 2 THzï¼Œå…¶è¾“å‡ºåŠŸç‡å·²æé«˜åˆ°æ¥è¿‘æ¯«ç“¦çš„æ°´å¹³ã€‚ä¸ºäº†è¿›ä¸€æ­¥æé«˜è¾“å‡ºåŠŸç‡ï¼Œè¿˜å¯¹ RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨é˜µåˆ—è¿›è¡Œäº†ç ”ç©¶ï¼Œæœ€è¿‘ï¼Œåœ¨ 36 ä¸ªå…ƒä»¶çš„æŒ¯è¡å™¨é˜µåˆ—ä¸­æŠ¥é“äº† 11.8 mW çš„æœ€é«˜è®°å½•è¾“å‡ºåŠŸç‡ã€‚

III æ—æ°®åŒ–ç‰©ææ–™å…·æœ‰å®½å¸¦åç§»ã€é«˜çƒ­å¯¼ç‡ã€é«˜å‡»ç©¿ç”µå‹ç­‰ä¼˜ç‚¹ï¼Œå…·æœ‰å®ç°é«˜åŠŸç‡å’Œé«˜å¯é æ€§ RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨çš„æ½œåŠ›ã€‚å‡ åå¹´æ¥ï¼Œä¸€äº›ç ”ç©¶å°ç»„ä¸€ç›´åœ¨ç ”ç©¶åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTDã€‚ç¬¬ä¸€ä¸ªåŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTD äº 2001 å¹´æŠ¥é“ï¼Œç„¶è€Œï¼Œæ—©æœŸçš„ç ”ç©¶åœ¨ç”µæµ-ç”µå‹ (I-V) ç‰¹æ€§æ–¹é¢ç¼ºä¹å¯é‡å¤æ€§ï¼Œå› ä¸ºåœ¨é‡å¤çš„ I-V æµ‹é‡è¿‡ç¨‹ä¸­ï¼Œè´Ÿå¾®åˆ†ç”µé˜» (NDR) ä¼šæ¶ˆå¤±ã€‚æœ€è¿‘ï¼Œäººä»¬æŠ¥é“äº†å…·æœ‰ç¨³å®š NDR åŠ¨ä½œçš„åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTDï¼Œå¹¶ä¸”å®ƒä»¬åœ¨å³°å€¼ç”µæµå¯†åº¦å’Œå³°è°·ç”µæµæ¯” (PVCR) æ–¹é¢å·²æ¥è¿‘å®ç”¨æ°´å¹³ã€‚äººä»¬å·²ç»è¿›è¡Œäº†ä¸€äº›ç ”ç©¶æ¥å®ç°åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨ï¼ŒåŒ…æ‹¬å¯¹ RTD å“åº”æ€§èƒ½çš„è¯„ä¼°ï¼Œä»¥åŠä½¿ç”¨è¿æ¥åˆ°å¤–éƒ¨ç”µè·¯çš„ RTD çš„æŒ¯è¡æ¼”ç¤ºã€‚ç„¶è€Œï¼Œå•ç‰‡é›†æˆçš„åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨å°šæœªå®ç°ã€‚

RTD è¦æ±‚ç²¾ç¡®çš„åšåº¦æ§åˆ¶å’Œé‡å­é˜±å’ŒåŠ¿å’çš„æ™¶ä½“è´¨é‡ï¼Œä»¥å®ç°æœ‰æ•ˆçš„è°æŒ¯éš§ç©¿ã€‚å› æ­¤ï¼Œå¤§å¤šæ•° RTD ç ”ç©¶ï¼ˆåŒ…æ‹¬æ°®åŒ–ç‰©å’Œç ·åŒ–ç‰©ææ–™ï¼‰éƒ½æ˜¯ä½¿ç”¨åˆ†å­æŸå¤–å»¶ (MBE) æ–¹æ³•è¿›è¡Œçš„ï¼Œä¸é‡‘å±æœ‰æœºåŒ–å­¦æ°”ç›¸æ²‰ç§¯ (MOCVD) ç›¸æ¯”ï¼Œè¯¥æ–¹æ³•å¯ä»¥å®ç°æ›´ç²¾ç¡®çš„åšåº¦æ§åˆ¶ã€‚ç„¶è€Œï¼Œè¦è·å¾—è‰¯å¥½çš„ RTD ç‰¹æ€§ï¼Œéœ€è¦åœ¨åŸå­çº§ä¸Šå®ç°å±‚åšåº¦çš„ç²¾ç¡®æ§åˆ¶ï¼Œä»¥åŠé˜±å’ŒåŠ¿å’ä¹‹é—´ç•Œé¢å±‚ä¹‹é—´çš„é™¡å³­å¼‚è´¨ç•Œé¢ã€‚å°½ç®¡å¦‚æ­¤ï¼ŒMOCVD ç”±äºå…¶é«˜ç”Ÿäº§ç‡å’Œèƒ½å¤Ÿç”Ÿäº§é«˜è´¨é‡æ™¶ä½“çš„èƒ½åŠ›è€Œè¢«å¹¿æ³›ç”¨äºå„ç§åŒ–åˆç‰©åŠå¯¼ä½“å™¨ä»¶ï¼ˆåŒ…æ‹¬å…‰å­¦å’Œç”µå­å™¨ä»¶ï¼‰çš„åˆ¶é€ ã€‚å¦‚æœåœ¨ MOCVD ä¸­å»ºç«‹äº†ç”Ÿé•¿æ¡ä»¶ï¼Œåˆ™å¯ä»¥é¢„æœŸè·å¾—è‰¯å¥½çš„ RTD ç‰¹æ€§ã€‚

ç„¶è€Œï¼Œä»¥å‰äººä»¬å·²ç»ä½¿ç”¨ InGaAs/AlAs RTD å¯¹åŸºäº MMIC çš„ RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨è¿›è¡Œäº†ç ”ç©¶ã€‚é€šè¿‡å°†å®ƒä»¬ç”¨äºåŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTDï¼Œå¯ä»¥é€šè¿‡ç”µæ°”è¯„ä¼°æŒ¯è¡ç‰¹æ€§ï¼Œä»è€Œèƒ½å¤Ÿè¯„ä¼°å¹¿æ³›çš„æŒ¯è¡é¢‘ç‡ï¼Œè€Œæ— éœ€ç‰¹æ®Šè¯„ä¼°æ–¹æ³•ã€‚

åœ¨è¿™ç¯‡è®ºæ–‡ä¸­ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬å±•ç¤ºäº†ä½¿ç”¨ MOCVD ç”Ÿé•¿çš„åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTD åŠå…¶é‡‡ç”¨ MMIC çš„æŒ¯è¡å™¨ã€‚æ‰€ç ”ç©¶çš„åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTD å¤–å»¶ç»“æ„åŒ…å«ä¸€ä¸ªåšåº¦ä¸º 2.0 nm çš„æ°®åŒ–é•“é‡å­é˜±å’Œåšåº¦ä¸º 1.5 nm çš„æ°®åŒ–é“åŒåŠ¿å’ã€‚è¯¥ç»“æ„åœ¨è‡ªç”±æ‚¬æµ®çš„ c é¢åŠç»ç¼˜æ°®åŒ–é•“è¡¬åº•ä¸Šç”Ÿé•¿ã€‚ä¸ºäº†åœ¨ MOCVD ä¸­ç”šè‡³æé«˜å¯æ§æ€§å’Œç»“æ™¶åº¦ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬ä¼˜åŒ–äº†ç”Ÿé•¿æ¡ä»¶å¹¶é‡‡ç”¨äº†å¼‚è´¨ç•Œé¢å¤„ç†æŠ€æœ¯ã€‚è¿™äº›åŠªåŠ›ä½¿æˆ‘ä»¬è·å¾—äº†å¦‚å›¾ 1(a) æ‰€ç¤ºçš„æ‰«æé€å°„ç”µå­æ˜¾å¾®é•œ (STEM) å›¾åƒæ‰€ç¤ºçš„ä¼˜è‰¯ AlN/GaN/AIN è¶…è–„è†œã€‚å¦‚å›¾ 1(b) æ‰€ç¤ºï¼ŒRTD ç»“æ„é‡‡ç”¨å¹²æ³•åˆ»èš€å½¢æˆçš„å°é¢ç»“æ„è¿›è¡Œåˆ¶å¤‡ã€‚åœ¨å°é¢çš„é¡¶éƒ¨å’Œåº•éƒ¨åˆ†åˆ«æ²‰ç§¯äº† Ti/Pt/Au ä½œä¸ºé›†ç”µæå’Œå‘å°„æã€‚å›¾ 1(c) æ˜¾ç¤ºäº†å…·æœ‰ 3 Âµm ç›´å¾„å°é¢çš„ GaN/AIN RTD æ ·å“çš„ä»£è¡¨æ€§ I-V ç‰¹æ€§ã€‚åœ¨ 4.7-5.2 V çš„ç”µå‹èŒƒå›´å†…è§‚å¯Ÿåˆ° NDR åŒºåŸŸï¼Œå…¶å³°å€¼ç”µæµå¯†åº¦çº¦ä¸º 200 kA/cmÂ²ï¼ŒPVCR ä¸º 1.52ã€‚åœ¨ RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨ç”µè·¯ä¸­ï¼ŒRTD çš„è´Ÿç”µé˜»ç”¨ä½œå¢ç›Šï¼ŒæŠµæ¶ˆäº†ç”µè·¯çš„åŠŸè€—å¹¶ç»´æŒæŒ¯è¡ã€‚å› æ­¤ï¼ŒRTD çš„è´Ÿç”µå¯¼åº”å¤§äºç”µè·¯çš„è´Ÿç”µå¯¼ã€‚è®¡ç®—å¾—å‡ºçš„è´Ÿç”µå¯¼ä¸º 14 mSï¼Œè¡¨ç¤ºä¸º (3/2)(Î”I/Î”V)ï¼Œå…¶ä¸­ Î”I å’Œ Î”V åˆ†åˆ«å®šä¹‰ä¸º NDR åŒºåŸŸä¸­å³°å€¼ç”µæµå’Œè°·å€¼ç”µæµä¹‹é—´çš„å·®å€¼ä»¥åŠå³°å€¼ç”µå‹å’Œè°·å€¼ç”µå‹ä¹‹é—´çš„å·®å€¼ã€‚RTD è¡¨ç°å‡ºä¼˜å¼‚çš„ I-V ç‰¹æ€§é‡å¤æ€§ï¼Œé¢„è®¡å¯åœ¨æŒ¯è¡å™¨ä¸­ä½œä¸ºè´Ÿç”µé˜»å…ƒä»¶ç¨³å®šè¿è¡Œã€‚

å›¾ 2(a) æ˜¯æ‰€åˆ¶å¤‡çš„åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTD-MMIC æŒ¯è¡å™¨çš„ç¤ºæ„å›¾ã€‚è¯¥å™¨ä»¶åŒ…æ‹¬ä¸€ä¸ªå…·æœ‰ 3 Âµm ç›´å¾„å°é¢çš„ RTDã€é‡‘å±-ç»ç¼˜ä½“-é‡‘å± (MIM) ç”µå®¹å™¨ã€å…±é¢æ³¢å¯¼ (CPW) å’Œåˆ†æµç”µé˜»ã€‚è¿™äº›ç”µè·¯å…ƒä»¶ä½¿ç”¨æ ‡å‡†å™¨ä»¶å·¥è‰ºæ–¹æ³•åœ¨åŠç»ç¼˜æ°®åŒ–é•“è¡¬åº•ä¸Šå•ç‰‡é›†æˆã€‚MIM ç”µå®¹å™¨é‡‡ç”¨å¤¹åœ¨ä¿¡å·å’Œæ¥åœ°é‡‘å±ä¹‹é—´çš„ 200 nm åšçš„äºŒæ°§åŒ–ç¡…å±‚ï¼Œä¿¡å·å’Œæ¥åœ°é‡‘å±æ˜¯é›†ç”µæå’Œå‘å°„æé‡‘å±çš„åŒé‡ä½œç”¨ã€‚åˆ†æµç”µé˜»é€šè¿‡é€‰æ‹©æ€§åœ°ä¿ç•™ n-GaN å‘å°„æå±‚è€Œå½¢æˆï¼Œæ²¡æœ‰è¿›è¡Œåˆ»èš€ï¼Œè¿™æœ‰åŠ©äºæŠ‘åˆ¶ç”µè·¯ä¸­çš„å¯„ç”ŸæŒ¯è¡å¹¶ä½¿æ‰€éœ€æŒ¯è¡ç¨³å®šã€‚è¯¥å™¨ä»¶çš„ç­‰æ•ˆç”µè·¯å¦‚å›¾ 2(b) æ‰€ç¤ºã€‚RTD è¢«è¡¨ç¤ºä¸ºè´Ÿç”µå¯¼ -Ga å’Œç”µå®¹ Cd çš„å¹¶è”ç”µè·¯ã€‚Lw æ˜¯ CPW çš„ç”µæ„Ÿï¼ŒC æ˜¯ MIM ç”µå®¹å™¨çš„ç”µå®¹ï¼ŒGs æ˜¯åˆ†æµç”µé˜»çš„ç”µå¯¼ã€‚ä¼ è¾“çº¿çš„ç”µé˜»ã€CPW çš„ç”µå®¹ä»¥åŠå…¶ä»–å„ç§ç”µè·¯å…ƒä»¶åœ¨æ­¤å¤„çœç•¥ï¼Œç›®çš„æ˜¯ä¸ºäº†ç®€åŒ–ã€‚ç”±äº MIM ç”µå®¹å™¨çš„è®¾è®¡ç›®çš„æ˜¯åˆ‡æ–­ç›´æµæˆ–ä½é¢‘ä¿¡å·å¹¶é€šè¿‡é«˜é¢‘ä¿¡å·ï¼Œå› æ­¤å¯¹äºé¢„æœŸ RF ä¿¡å·ï¼Œå®ƒå¯ä»¥è¢«è§†ä¸ºçŸ­è·¯ï¼Œå› æ­¤å¯ä»¥ç®€åŒ–å›¾ 2(b) æ‰€ç¤ºçš„ç­‰æ•ˆç”µè·¯ã€‚å¯ä»¥ç®€åŒ–è¯¥ç”µè·¯ï¼Œå¦‚å›¾ 2(c) æ‰€ç¤ºã€‚å› æ­¤ï¼ŒæŒ¯è¡é¢‘ç‡ä¸»è¦ç”± Lw å’Œ Ca å†³å®šã€‚ä½¿ç”¨ä¸‰ç»´ç”µç£æ¨¡æ‹Ÿå™¨ (Ansys HFSS) å’Œç”µè·¯æ¨¡æ‹Ÿå™¨ (Keysight ADS) è®¡ç®— MIM çš„é¢ç§¯å’Œ CPW çš„é•¿åº¦ï¼Œè¿™ä¸¤ä¸ªå‚æ•°å†³å®šäº†ç”µè·¯çš„æˆªæ­¢é¢‘ç‡å’Œç”µæ„Ÿï¼Œä»è€Œä½¿æŒ¯è¡é¢‘ç‡åœ¨ 10-20 GHz çš„èŒƒå›´å†…ã€‚å›¾ 2(d) æ˜¾ç¤ºäº†ç”µè·¯é˜»æŠ—çš„é¢‘ç‡ä¾èµ–æ€§ï¼ŒåŒ…æ‹¬ RTD ç”µè·¯ä¿¡æ¯ã€‚ä¼°è®¡çš„æŒ¯è¡é¢‘ç‡çº¦ä¸º 16 GHzï¼Œå…¶ä¸­é˜»æŠ—çš„è™šéƒ¨ Im{Y}ï¼ˆå³ç”µè·¯çš„ç”µçº³ï¼‰å˜ä¸ºé›¶ã€‚åœ¨ä¼°è®¡çš„æŒ¯è¡é¢‘ç‡ä¸‹ï¼Œç”µè·¯çš„ç”µå¯¼ Re{Y} ä¸º 6.6 mSï¼Œæ˜æ˜¾å°äº RTD çš„è´Ÿç”µå¯¼ 14 mSï¼Œå› æ­¤ RTD é¢„è®¡å°†ä½œä¸ºè´Ÿç”µé˜»å…ƒä»¶æ¥æŠµæ¶ˆæŒ¯è¡ç”µè·¯çš„å¯„ç”Ÿç”µé˜»ã€‚

ä½¿ç”¨é¢‘è°±åˆ†æä»ªåœ¨æ™¶åœ†ä¸Šæµ‹é‡äº†æ‰€åˆ¶å¤‡ç”µè·¯çš„æŒ¯è¡é¢‘ç‡ã€‚ä½¿ç”¨ GSG æ¢é’ˆä»ä¸€ä¾§ (å›¾ 2(a) ä¸­å™¨ä»¶çš„å·¦ä¾§) å¯¹å™¨ä»¶æ–½åŠ ç›´æµç”µå‹ï¼Œå¹¶ä»å¦ä¸€ä¾§ (å³ä¾§) æµ‹é‡æŒ¯è¡ã€‚å›¾ 3 æ˜¾ç¤ºäº†æµ‹é‡çš„é¢‘è°±ã€‚åœ¨çº¦ 17 GHz çš„åŸºé¢‘å¤„æˆåŠŸå®ç°äº†æŒ¯è¡ï¼Œè¿™ä¸æ¨¡æ‹Ÿä¸­ä¼°è®¡çš„é¢‘ç‡åŸºæœ¬ä¸€è‡´ã€‚å›¾ä¸­æ’å›¾æ˜¾ç¤ºäº†å™¨ä»¶çš„ I-V ç‰¹æ€§ã€‚I-V æ›²çº¿ç”±æµè¿‡ RTD å’Œåˆ†æµç”µé˜»çš„ç”µæµåˆ†é‡çš„æ€»å’Œè¡¨ç¤ºã€‚æµ‹é‡æŒ¯è¡é¢‘è°±çš„æ–½åŠ ç”µå‹è¢«è®¾å®šåœ¨ NDR åŒºåŸŸçš„ä¸­å¿ƒã€‚åœ¨æ›´é«˜çš„é¢‘ç‡ä¸‹ï¼Œå¿…é¡»æ”¹è¿› RTD çš„ç‰¹æ€§ï¼Œå¦‚è´Ÿå¾®åˆ†ç”µå¯¼ã€æ¥è§¦ç”µé˜»å’Œè–„å±‚ç”µé˜»ï¼Œå¹¶ä¸”å¿…é¡»ä¼˜åŒ–æŒ¯è¡å™¨è®¾è®¡ã€‚é€šè¿‡ä¼˜åŒ–æ™¶ä½“ç»“æ„ã€MOCVD ç”Ÿé•¿æ¡ä»¶å’Œå·¥è‰ºæ¡ä»¶ï¼Œé¢„è®¡å¯ä»¥æ”¹å–„ RTD çš„è¿™äº›ç‰¹æ€§ã€‚

æ€»ä¹‹ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬å¼€å‘äº†åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨ï¼Œä»¥å®ç°æ¯«ç±³æ³¢å’Œå¤ªèµ«å…¹åº”ç”¨çš„é«˜åŠŸç‡å’Œé«˜å¯é æ€§å…‰æºï¼Œå¹¶ä¸”æˆ‘ä»¬å·²ç»æ¼”ç¤ºäº†å…·æœ‰ 17 GHz åŸºé¢‘çš„åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTD åŠå…¶æŒ¯è¡å™¨ã€‚ä½¿ç”¨ MOCVD å®ç°äº†å…·æœ‰ç²¾ç¡®åšåº¦æ§åˆ¶å’Œé™¡å³­é˜±/åŠ¿å’å¼‚è´¨ç•Œé¢çš„ GaN/AIN RTDã€‚æŒ¯è¡ç”µè·¯åŒ…æ‹¬åœ¨åŠç»ç¼˜æ°®åŒ–é•“è¡¬åº•ä¸Šå•ç‰‡é›†æˆçš„å…·æœ‰ 3 Âµm ç›´å¾„å°é¢çš„ RTDã€CPWã€MIM ç”µå®¹å™¨å’Œåˆ†æµç”µé˜»ã€‚ä½¿ç”¨ä¸‰ç»´ç”µç£æ¨¡æ‹Ÿå™¨ HFSS å’Œç”µè·¯æ¨¡æ‹Ÿå™¨ ADS è®¾è®¡äº†æŒ¯è¡ç”µè·¯ï¼Œå¹¶ä¸”ä¼°è®¡çš„æŒ¯è¡é¢‘ç‡ä¸å®éªŒç»“æœå¯†åˆ‡åŒ¹é…ã€‚ä¸ºäº†è¿›ä¸€æ­¥æ”¹è¿›æŒ¯è¡ç‰¹æ€§ï¼Œéœ€è¦é‡‡ç”¨åŒæ—¶å…³æ³¨æ”¹è¿› RTD ç‰¹æ€§å¹¶ä¼˜åŒ–æŒ¯è¡å™¨è®¾è®¡çš„åŒé‡æ–¹æ³•ã€‚é€šè¿‡ä¼˜åŒ–æ™¶ä½“ç»“æ„ã€MOCVD ç”Ÿé•¿æ¡ä»¶å’Œå·¥è‰ºæ¡ä»¶ï¼Œé¢„è®¡å¯ä»¥è¿›ä¸€æ­¥æ”¹è¿› RTD çš„ç‰¹æ€§ã€‚III æ—æ°®åŒ–ç‰©åŠå¯¼ä½“æ˜¯å¾ˆæœ‰å¸å¼•åŠ›çš„ææ–™ï¼Œä¸ºæœªæ¥å®ç°é«˜è¾“å‡ºå’Œé«˜å¯é æ€§ RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨é“ºå¹³äº†é“è·¯ã€‚åŸºäºæ°®åŒ–é•“çš„ RTD æŒ¯è¡å™¨çš„è¿›æ­¥å¿…å°†æœ‰åŠ©äºæ¯«ç±³æ³¢å’Œå¤ªèµ«å…¹å…‰æºçš„è¿›ä¸€æ­¥æ™®åŠã€‚

## 19.3 RTD-DRAM

RTD-DRAMï¼ˆResonant Tunneling Diode Dynamic Random Access Memoryï¼‰æ˜¯ä¸€ç§åˆ©ç”¨å…±æŒ¯éš§ç©¿äºŒæç®¡ï¼ˆRTDï¼‰ç‰¹æ€§è®¾è®¡çš„æ–°å‹åŠ¨æ€éšæœºå­˜å–å­˜å‚¨å™¨ï¼ˆDRAMï¼‰ã€‚å®ƒç»“åˆäº†RTDçš„è´Ÿå¾®åˆ†ç”µé˜»ç‰¹æ€§ä¸ä¼ ç»ŸDRAMçš„å­˜å‚¨ç»“æ„ï¼Œæ—¨åœ¨æé«˜DRAMçš„é€Ÿåº¦ã€åŠŸè€—å’Œå¯†åº¦æ€§èƒ½ã€‚

RTD-DRAM çš„å·¥ä½œåŸç†ï¼š

å…±æŒ¯éš§ç©¿äºŒæç®¡ (RTD) çš„è´Ÿå¾®åˆ†ç”µé˜»ç‰¹æ€§ï¼š RTD çš„ç”µæµ-ç”µå‹æ›²çº¿æœ‰ä¸€ä¸ªè´Ÿå¾®åˆ†ç”µé˜»åŒºåŸŸï¼Œç”µæµåœ¨æ­¤åŒºéšç€ç”µå‹çš„å¢åŠ è€Œå‡å°ã€‚åˆ©ç”¨è¿™ç§ç‰¹æ€§ï¼ŒRTD-DRAM å¯ä»¥é€šè¿‡å…±æŒ¯éš§ç©¿æ¥åŠ é€Ÿç”µè·å†™å…¥å’Œè¯»å‡ºè¿‡ç¨‹ã€‚

æ›´ä½çš„åŠŸè€—ï¼š ç”±äº RTD çš„è´Ÿå¾®åˆ†ç”µé˜»ç‰¹æ€§ï¼Œåœ¨æŸäº›å·¥ä½œåŒºé—´å†…ï¼Œå™¨ä»¶åŠŸè€—è¾ƒä½ï¼Œè¿™ä½¿å¾— RTD-DRAM æ¯”ä¼ ç»Ÿ DRAM æ›´èŠ‚èƒ½ã€‚

## 31.4 åˆ°2030å¹´å–ä»£æ‰‹æœºä¸­çš„GaAs

åœ¨è¿‡å»çš„30å¹´é‡Œï¼ŒGaAså¾®ç”µå­æŠ€æœ¯çš„å‘å±•æœºé‡æ—¥ç›Šç¼©å‡ã€‚åœ¨20ä¸–çºªçš„æœ€ååå¹´ï¼Œæ•°å­—GaAsåº”ç”¨äºå…‰ç½‘ç»œåŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½ï¼Œé©±åŠ¨ç€ä¸€ç³»åˆ—å…ƒä»¶ï¼ŒåŒ…æ‹¬æ¿€å…‰å™¨ã€è·¨é˜»æ”¾å¤§å™¨å’Œå¤šè·¯å¤ç”¨å™¨ã€‚åœ¨äº’è”ç½‘æ³¡æ²«ç ´ç­åï¼Œç¡…å’ŒSiGeå…ƒä»¶å æ®äº†ä¸»å¯¼åœ°ä½ï¼Œå°„é¢‘é¢†åŸŸå æ®äº†GaAsæ™¶ä½“ç®¡çš„å…¨éƒ¨é”€å”®é¢ã€‚è™½ç„¶å›½é˜²å’Œç½‘ç»œåŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½ä¹Ÿå¸¦æ¥äº†ä¸€äº›æ”¶å…¥ï¼Œä½†æ‰‹æœºå æ®äº†æœ€å¤§çš„ä»½é¢ã€‚æœ€åˆï¼ŒGaAs pHEMTæä¾›å¼€å…³åŠŸèƒ½ï¼Œåæ¥è¢«ç»ç¼˜ä½“ä¸Šç¡…æŠ€æœ¯å–ä»£ï¼ŒGaAsçš„ä¸»è¦ä½œç”¨æ˜¯åŠŸç‡æ”¾å¤§ã€‚ä½†ç°åœ¨ï¼Œè¿™ä¸€åœ°ä½æ­£å—åˆ°å¨èƒï¼Œç¾å›½å…¬å¸Finwaveé¢„æµ‹ï¼Œåˆ°2020å¹´ï¼ŒGaNå°†åœ¨æ‰‹æœºä¸­æ‰¿æ‹…è¿™ä¸€ä»»åŠ¡ï¼ŒåŒæ—¶ï¼ŒGaNä½œä¸ºå¼€å…³å’ŒåŠŸç‡æ”¾å¤§å™¨åœ¨åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½ã€èˆªç©ºèˆªå¤©å’Œå›½é˜²åº”ç”¨ä¸­çš„åº”ç”¨ä¹Ÿå°†å¸¦æ¥é¢å¤–çš„é”€å”®é¢ã€‚

## 31.6 GaN (Gallium Nitride) Research Report Summary

**Market Growth and Forecasts**

- The GaN power device market is experiencing rapid expansion, with Yole Group projecting it to surpass $2 billion by 2029, driven by a strong compound annual growth rate (CAGR) of approximately 41% from 2023 to 2029[6][7].
- The overall compound semiconductor device market, which includes GaN and SiC, is expected to grow at nearly 13% CAGR, reaching about $25 billion by 2030, outpacing the broader semiconductor market[6].
- GaNâ€™s share of the global power device market is forecast to increase significantly, with wide bandgap materials (including GaN and SiC) expected to account for over 32% of the market by 2029, up from 16% in 2024[7].

**Key Application Areas**

- **Consumer Electronics**: GaN is widely adopted in high-efficiency, compact chargers (up to 300W), home appliance power supplies, and motor drives, offering better efficiency and miniaturization[4].
- **Automotive**: GaN is gaining traction in electric vehicles (EVs), particularly for on-board chargers and power conversion systems, supported by the global shift to electrification and carbon reduction[7].
- **Data Centers and Telecom**: GaNâ€™s high-frequency and high-efficiency characteristics make it attractive for data center power supplies and 5G telecom infrastructure[4][5].
- **RF (Radio Frequency) Applications**: GaN RF devices are growing at a 12% CAGR, expected to reach over $2 billion by 2025, with primary drivers being telecom (5G, satellite communications) and defense (radar, AESA systems)[8].

**Industry Trends and Competitive Landscape**

- Major players in the power GaN market as of 2025 include Innoscience, Power Integrations, and Navitas, with Infineon and Renesas expanding through acquisitions of GaN Systems and Transphorm, respectively[5][6].
- There is increasing synergy between GaN power and RF applications, with companies leveraging existing production infrastructure for both segments[5][6].
- The supply chain is evolving, with vertical integration and strategic collaborations to reduce dependencies and address geopolitical risks[5][6].

**Technology and Market Drivers**

- The rapid adoption of SiC in automotive has paved the way for GaNâ€™s rise, especially as OEMs seek higher efficiency and power density in new applications[5][6].
- Investments in wide bandgap technologies are substantial, with more than $30 billion announced globally for SiC, and similar momentum building for GaN[7].
- GaNâ€™s advantages include higher efficiency, smaller size, and the ability to operate at higher frequencies and voltages compared to traditional silicon devices[4][7].

**Challenges and Outlook**

- While GaN is well established in consumer and telecom sectors, broader adoption in automotive and industrial markets will depend on further cost reduction and supply chain maturity[4][7].
- The market is expected to continue its strong growth trajectory, with new applications in AI-driven data centers, renewable energy, and high-performance automotive systems providing additional momentum[5][7].

---

In summary, GaN technology is at an inflection point, moving from niche to mainstream across multiple high-growth sectors. Its market is set for robust expansion through the end of the decade, underpinned by technological advantages, expanding applications, and strategic industry shifts[6][7][4].

## 31.7 Gallium Nitride (GaN) Multi-Market Analysis: Power, Optoelectronics, and RF  

### Power Electronics Market  
- **Market Growth**: GaN power devices are projected to grow from **USD 22.2B (2024)** to **USD 40.9B by 2034** (6.4% CAGR)[2], with broader GaN markets reaching **USD 7.95B by 2033** (15.7% CAGR)[13].  
- **Key Drivers**:  
  - **Consumer Electronics**: Dominates with GaN-based fast chargers (300W+) and compact power adapters, driven by demand for higher efficiency and miniaturization[2][6].  
  - **Automotive**: Adoption in 11kW onboard chargers (OBCs) and EV powertrains, leveraging GaNâ€™s high thermal stability and power density[10][13].  
  - **Renewables**: Solar inverters and energy storage systems benefit from GaNâ€™s reduced conduction losses and higher switching speeds[13].  

---

### Optoelectronics Market  
- **Market Leadership**: Opto-semiconductors held **36.3% revenue share (2024)**, led by LEDs, LiDAR, and UV lasers[10].  
- **Applications**:  
  - **Solid-State Lighting**: GaN-based LEDs enable energy-efficient white lighting, with phosphor-converted designs reducing reliance on traditional bulbs[1][9].  
  - **LiDAR**: Critical for autonomous vehicles, leveraging GaNâ€™s high electron mobility for precise pulsed lasers[10].  
  - **Displays**: Blue/green LEDs for micro-LED displays and large panels, addressing brightness and color accuracy challenges[1].  
- **Innovations**: Projects like DENIS improved GaN substrate quality, enhancing LED luminous efficacy and device longevity[9].  

---

### RF (Radio Frequency) Market  
- **Explosive Growth**: RF GaN market to expand from **USD 1.68B (2024)** to **USD 8.22B by 2033** (19.3% CAGR)[4], with defense and telecom as primary drivers.  
- **Key Segments**:  
  - **5G Infrastructure**: GaN-on-SiC dominates macro/microcell base stations, enabling massive MIMO and mmWave systems with >45% market share by 2028[7].  
  - **Defense**: Radar, electronic warfare, and satellite communications rely on GaNâ€™s high power density and radiation hardness[4][7].  
  - **Satellite Comms**: GaN enhances signal strength and efficiency in transceivers, critical for LEO/geostationary networks[3][8].  
- **Technology Shift**: GaN-on-Si gains traction in low-power telecom (e.g., small cells), reducing costs while maintaining performance[7].  

---

### Cross-Sector Advantages  
| **Property**       | **Power**              | **Optoelectronics**    | **RF**                 |  
|---------------------|------------------------|------------------------|------------------------|  
| **Bandgap**         | 3.4 eV (high breakdown)| Enables UV/blue emission| High-frequency operation|  
| **Thermal Conductivity** | Reduces cooling needs | Improves LED lifespan  | Enhances radar reliability |  
| **Efficiency**      | >99% in converters     | 50% energy savings vs. bulbs| 30% higher PA efficiency vs. LDMOS |  

---

### Industry Outlook  
- **Power**: Cost parity with silicon in consumer electronics achieved; industrial/auto adoption hinges on further cost reductions[13].  
- **Opto**: Micro-LED and AR/VR displays to drive next growth phase, with LiDAR demand accelerating[10].  
- **RF**: 6G R&D and satellite mega-constellations (e.g., Starlink) will sustain 20%+ CAGRs through 2030[4][8].  
- **Key Players**: Wolfspeed, Qorvo, and Infineon lead in GaN power/RF[6][7], while Samsung and Apple push opto-innovation[9][10].  

GaNâ€™s versatility across power, opto, and RF sectors positions it as a cornerstone of next-gen electronics, driven by material advantages and synergistic industry investments.

## 31.10 Status of the Compound Semiconductor Industry Report â€” Yole Intelligence, 2025

### Market Size and Growth

- The compound semiconductor device market is projected to reach **$25 billion by 2030**, growing at a robust **CAGR of nearly 13%** from 2024, significantly outpacing the overall semiconductor market[1][2][3][5][6].
- In 2024, the compound semiconductor market is a small but fast-growing segment within the broader $670 billion semiconductor device industry[1].
- Growth is primarily driven by **automotive and mobility (especially EVs and ADAS)**, with strong momentum also from **telecom, infrastructure, and consumer electronics**[1][2][3][5][6].

### Key Application Areas

- **Power Electronics:**  
  - SiC (Silicon Carbide) is widely adopted in electric vehicles (EVs) for power devices.
  - GaN (Gallium Nitride) is gaining traction in power electronics, especially for DC/DC converters, onboard chargers (OBCs), and LiDAR in automotive applications[1][2][3][5].
- **RF (Radio Frequency):**  
  - RF GaAs remains dominant in consumer applications but faces geopolitical and supply chain challenges.
  - RF GaN, initially developed for defense, is now critical in 5G and satellite communications[1][2][3][5].
- **Photonics:**  
  - Growth in photonics is fueled by AI and datacom, with InP and GaAs devices seeing increased collaboration and demand.
  - Automotive LiDAR is accelerating adoption of compound semiconductor-based lasers[1][2].
- **Displays & Lighting:**  
  - The microLED display industry is growing, though still fragmented, with major display makers securing LED supply and startups driving innovation[1][5].

### Industry Trends and Dynamics

- **Strategic Moves:**  
  - Major semiconductor players are increasing investments in compound technologies, with companies like Infineon, STMicroelectronics, onsemi, and Wolfspeed adopting vertically integrated models to secure supply and reduce geopolitical risks[2][5].
  - The SiC boom has led to consolidation and specialization, while GaN is seen as the next major breakthrough, especially in power and RF applications[3][5].
- **Synergies and Collaborations:**  
  - Companies are leveraging synergies between GaN power and RF applications, optimizing production infrastructure and epitaxy equipment[3][5].
  - The supply chain is evolving, with strategic collaborations and regional investments to address supply security and technological advancement[1][2][5].
- **Geographical Trends:**  
  - Asia-Pacific continues to lead in manufacturing and R&D, while Europe and the US are increasing local investments to mitigate supply chain risks[4].

### Technology and Competitive Landscape

- The report provides detailed forecasts for **device and bare die market values, shipments, and technology adoption** across power, RF, photonics, and display applications[5][6].
- It also examines the competition between compound semiconductors and mature silicon technologies, highlighting manufacturing challenges and emerging innovations[5][6].
- Key players include Wolfspeed, Infineon, STMicroelectronics, onsemi, and others, with new entrants and startups driving innovation in niche areas[2][5][6].

---

**Summary:**  
The 2025 Yole Intelligence report highlights a dynamic and rapidly growing compound semiconductor industry, set to exceed $25B by 2030. Growth is fueled by automotive electrification, AI, 5G, and advanced photonics, with SiC and GaN leading technological advances in power and RF. Strategic investments, supply chain evolution, and cross-sector collaborations are shaping the industry's future[1][2][3][5][6].

[5] https://www.yolegroup.com/press-release/compound-semiconductors-strategic-moves-collaborations-in-a-nutshell/

PSï¼šæ˜¯çš„ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºGaNæŠ€æœ¯ç¡®å®æ˜¯ä¸€ä¸ªæ¨åŠ¨å› ç´ ã€‚å®ƒæä¾›äº†åœ¨æ•´ä¸ªå¼€å…³é¢‘ç‡ä¸‹å·¥ä½œçš„å¯èƒ½æ€§ï¼Œä»è€Œæé«˜äº†æ–°å‹æ¥æ”¶å™¨æ‰€éœ€çš„åŠŸç‡å¯†åº¦ã€‚ç›®å‰ï¼Œè®¡ç®—æ¥æ”¶å™¨çš„æ•°é‡è‡³å°‘ä»72ä¸ªå¼€å§‹ï¼Œä½†é¢„è®¡å¸‚åœºé¢†å¯¼è€…æ¨å‡ºçš„æ–°äº§å“æ•°é‡å°†ä¸Šå‡åˆ°500ä¸ªï¼Œæ¯”å¦‚GPUæ¥æ”¶å™¨ï¼Œå…¶åŠŸç‡é«˜è¾¾600åƒç“¦ï¼Œç”šè‡³é«˜è¾¾1å…†ç“¦/æ¥æ”¶å™¨ï¼Œä»¥åŠäº¤æµåˆ°ç›´æµçš„ä¾§æ¥æ”¶å™¨ã€‚å½“ç„¶ï¼Œä»è¿™ä¸ªæ„ä¹‰ä¸Šè®²ï¼Œå®ƒå¯ä»¥ç¼©å°ç©ºé—´ï¼Œåœ¨ç›¸åŒç©ºé—´å†…æé«˜åŠŸç‡ï¼Œå¤§çº¦ç›¸å½“äºæ¯ç«‹æ–¹è‹±å¯¸2000åˆ°3000ç“¦ã€‚æ‰€ä»¥ï¼ŒåŸºæœ¬ä¸Šï¼Œå¦‚æœè¦å®ç°é«˜å¯†åº¦ï¼ŒGaNæŠ€æœ¯å¯ä»¥å®ç°è¿™ä¸€ç‚¹ã€‚å½“ç„¶ï¼Œè¿™å¹¶éæ˜“äº‹ï¼Œå› ä¸ºå®ƒå…·æœ‰å¼€å…³èƒ½åŠ›ï¼Œæ²¡æœ‰åˆ†é›†ç¼–ç æŸè€—ï¼Œè€Œä¸”ä¸å…¶ä»–æŠ€æœ¯ç›¸æ¯”ï¼Œå®ƒçš„å¼€å…³æŸè€—æ›´ä½ï¼Œæ— è®ºæ˜¯åœ¨å¼€å…³æ‹“æ‰‘ç»“æ„ä¸­ï¼Œè¿˜æ˜¯åœ¨ç¡¬å¼€å…³ä¸­ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºè¿˜æœ‰å¦ä¸€ä¸ªæ¶æ„å…ƒç´ ï¼Œé‚£å°±æ˜¯åŒå‘å¼€å…³ã€‚è¯¥å™¨ä»¶å¯ä»¥å®ç°æ‹“æ‰‘ç»“æ„çš„æŸç§è½¬å˜ã€‚è¿™ç»å¯¹æ˜¯ä¸€ä¸ªé‡è¦çš„å…ƒç´ ï¼Œå› ä¸ºåœ¨äº¤æµ/ç›´æµè½¬æ¢æ–¹é¢ï¼Œè¿™å°†å¸¦æ¥å·¨å¤§çš„æ”¹å˜ï¼Œå› ä¸ºä½ å¯ä»¥è½»æ¾å®ç°ä¸¤ç§å¤šå±‚æ‹“æ‰‘ç»“æ„ï¼Œæˆ–è€…è¯´ï¼Œç®€åŒ–æ‹“æ‰‘ç»“æ„ä»¥é™ä½æŸè€—ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºè¿™å¯¹äºå–ä»£å…¶ä»–æŠ€æœ¯ï¼Œåœ¨æ›´å°çš„ç©ºé—´å†…ä»¥æ›´ä½çš„é€Ÿåº¦å®ç°ç›¸åŒçš„æ•ˆç‡è‡³å…³é‡è¦ã€‚

PSï¼šå½“ç„¶ã€‚æ”¶è´­Transphormæ˜¯ä¸€æ¬¡æ˜æ™ºçš„é€‰æ‹©ï¼Œç°åœ¨å‡ ä¹å®Œæˆäº†å…¨æ–¹ä½çš„æ•´åˆã€‚æ˜¾ç„¶ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬æ”¶è´­äº†ä¸€å®¶æ‹¥æœ‰è‰¯å¥½æŠ€æœ¯çš„å…¬å¸ï¼Œå®ƒç°åœ¨ä¸ä»…åœ¨è§„æ¨¡ä¸Šï¼Œè€Œä¸”åœ¨åˆ¶é€ æ–¹é¢ä¹Ÿå……åˆ†åˆ©ç”¨äº†ç‘è¨çš„è§„æ¨¡ä¼˜åŠ¿ï¼Œå› ä¸ºæˆ‘ä»¬æ˜¾ç„¶æ­£åœ¨æ‰“é€ å¤šåŒºåŸŸä¸šåŠ¡ï¼Œè¿™ä¹Ÿç¬¦åˆåœ¨ä¸‰å¤§æ´²é¡ºåˆ©è¿è¥çš„éœ€è¦ï¼Œæ¯”å¦‚è¯´åœ¨ä¸¤å¤§æ´²å¼€å±•ä¸šåŠ¡ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºï¼Œå°±åˆ¶é€ è€Œè¨€ï¼Œæ ¹æ®ä¸åŒçš„å¸‚åœºï¼Œæƒ…å†µä¼šæœ‰æ‰€ä¸åŒã€‚ä»Šå¤©æˆ‘ä»¬çœ‹åˆ°ï¼Œæ¨åŠ¨650èŠ¯ç‰‡å‘å±•çš„å¸‚åœºä¸»è¦æ˜¯ç‰©è”ç½‘å’Œæ¶ˆè´¹ç”µå­ï¼Œæ¯”å¦‚å……ç”µå™¨ï¼Œå¯¹å§ï¼Ÿä½†ç°åœ¨æˆ‘ä»¬çœ‹åˆ°äº†åŸºç¡€è®¾æ–½é¢†åŸŸçš„å·¨å¤§å‘å±•åŠ¿å¤´ï¼Œå› æ­¤ç”µæºè‚¯å®šéœ€è¦è¿™é¡¹æŠ€æœ¯ã€‚ä½†å®ƒç›®å‰è¿˜æ²¡æœ‰å®ç°è§„æ¨¡åŒ–ã€‚å› æ­¤ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬è·å¾—äº†è¿™ç§åŠ¿å¤´ï¼Œäº§é‡ä¹Ÿä¼šéšä¹‹å¢åŠ ï¼Œå› æ­¤8è‹±å¯¸æ™¶åœ†å°±æˆä¸ºæ”¯æŒè¿™ç§äº§é‡æ°´å¹³çš„å¿…éœ€å“ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºè¿˜æœ‰ä¸€ä¸ªå› ç´ ï¼Œå½“ç„¶æ˜¯æˆæœ¬ï¼Œå¯¹å§ï¼Ÿä»é•¿è¿œæ¥çœ‹ï¼ŒGaNæœ‰æ½œåŠ›æˆä¸ºç¡…çš„ç«äº‰å¯¹æ‰‹ã€‚å› ä¸ºç†è®ºä¸Šï¼ŒåŒæ ·çš„é¢ç§¯å¯ä»¥æ‰¿å—æ›´å¤§çš„åŠŸç‡ã€‚ä»è¿™ä¸ªæ„ä¹‰ä¸Šè®²ï¼Œå¦‚æœæ‹¿è‹¹æœå’Œè‹¹æœè¿›è¡Œæ¯”è¾ƒï¼Œæ‹¥æœ‰ç›¸åŒçš„æ™¶åœ†æ˜¯åŸºç¡€ï¼Œæœ€ç»ˆä¸ä»…èƒ½ä¸å…¶ä»–å®½å¸¦éš™ææ–™ç«äº‰ï¼Œä¹Ÿèƒ½ä¸ç¡…è¿›è¡Œäº¤å‰ç«äº‰ã€‚å› æ­¤ï¼Œ12è‹±å¯¸è‚¯å®šä¼šæˆä¸ºä¸€ä¸ªè½åœ°ç‚¹ã€‚ç›®å‰å°šä¸æ¸…æ¥šå…·ä½“æ—¶é—´ï¼Œä½†æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºè¿™åªæ˜¯å‡ å¹´çš„é—®é¢˜ï¼Œå› ä¸ºåˆ°é‚£æ—¶ï¼Œæˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºä»¥ç¡…ä½œä¸ºè¡¬åº•ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬éƒ½èƒ½åšåˆ°è¿™ä¸€ç‚¹ã€‚è¿™æ˜¯ä¸€ä¸ªæŠ•èµ„è§„æ¨¡çš„é—®é¢˜ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºå®æ–½è¿™ç§åˆ¶é€ æ–¹å¼éœ€è¦èµ„æœ¬æ”¯å‡ºã€‚

æˆ‘ï¼šæ‰€ä»¥ï¼Œè°ˆåˆ°GaNï¼Œåœ¨æ¨¡å¼ã€æ¨¡å¼å’Œæ¶æ„æ–¹é¢ä¹Ÿå­˜åœ¨ç€æ¿€çƒˆçš„äº‰è®ºã€‚ä»å¯é æ€§ç³»ç»Ÿé›†æˆçš„è§’åº¦æ¥çœ‹ï¼Œæ‚¨å¯¹è¿™ç§é€‰æ‹©å’Œè®¾è®¡é€‰æ‹©æŒä»€ä¹ˆç«‹åœºï¼Ÿå¯¹äºæ•°æ®ä¸­å¿ƒæ¥è¯´ï¼Œæœ€é‡è¦çš„æ˜¯é«˜å¯é æ€§å’Œåº”ç”¨ï¼Œä»¥åŠåœ¨æˆæœ¬ç»“æ„æ–¹é¢ï¼Ÿé‚£ä¹ˆï¼Œè¿™äº›è¦ç´ å’Œå› ç´ åœ¨Cascodeæ¨¡å¼å’Œå…¶ä»–ä¸åŒé›†æˆæ¨¡å¼çš„é€‰æ‹©ä¸­èµ·ç€ä»€ä¹ˆä½œç”¨ï¼Ÿæ‚¨æåˆ°äº†650ä¼ï¼Œè¿™ä¸ç¡…çš„ç«äº‰ï¼Œå¯èƒ½ä¼šæ”¹è¿›GaNæŠ€æœ¯ã€‚æˆ‘ä»¬ä¹Ÿå¯ä»¥è°ˆè°ˆä¸ç¢³åŒ–ç¡…çš„ç«äº‰ã€‚

PSï¼šæ˜¯çš„ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºè¿™å¯ä»¥è¯´æ˜¯ä»·å€¼ç™¾ä¸‡ç¾å…ƒçš„é—®é¢˜ä¹‹ä¸€ï¼Œå› ä¸ºæˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºï¼Œå½“ä½ å…·ä½“è°ˆè®ºä¸€é¡¹æ–°æŠ€æœ¯æ—¶ï¼Œè‚¯å®šä¼šæœ‰å„ç§ä¸åŒçš„æ–¹æ¡ˆï¼Œå„æœ‰ä¼˜ç¼ºç‚¹ã€‚æ‰€ä»¥æ²¡æœ‰ä¸€ç§ä¸‡èƒ½çš„è§£å†³æ–¹æ¡ˆã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºæˆ‘ä»¬çš„è§‚ç‚¹æ˜¯é«˜åŠŸç‡ã€é«˜ç”µå‹ä¸‹çš„æƒ…å†µã€‚å‡è®¾[çŸ­]å…ƒä»¶çš„å¯¼é€šç”µé˜»ä¸º650Î©ï¼Œæœ€ç»ˆè¾¾åˆ°æ›´é«˜æ°´å¹³æ—¶ä¼šæ›´é«˜ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºè€—å°½å‹ç”±äºå¤šç§åŸå› å…·æœ‰æ›´ä¼˜å¼‚çš„å“è´¨å› æ•°ã€‚é¦–å…ˆï¼Œæˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºå®ƒæ˜¯ä¸€ç§å®Œå…¨éš”ç¦»çš„æ …æï¼Œå› æ­¤å°±å™¨ä»¶çš„å¯é æ€§å’Œç¨³å¥æ€§è€Œè¨€ï¼Œè¿™æ˜¯ä¸€ä¸ªå¾ˆå¤§çš„é™„åŠ å€¼ã€‚å…¶æ¬¡ï¼Œå®ƒçš„æ¸©åº¦ä¾èµ–æ€§æ›´ä½ï¼Œå¯¹å§ï¼Ÿé€šå¸¸æƒ…å†µä¸‹ï¼Œè€—å°½å‹å¤§çº¦æ˜¯[å¯¼é€šç”µé˜»]éšæ¸©åº¦å‡é«˜è€Œå¢åŠ çš„ä¸€åŠã€‚ç„¶åï¼Œå®é™…ä¸Šï¼Œå¢å¼ºæ•ˆåº”ä¸ä»…ä½“ç°åœ¨å‚æ•°çš„é€’å¢ä¸Šï¼Œç‰¹åˆ«æ˜¯åŠ¨æ€å¯¼é€šç”µé˜»ï¼ˆRDS(on)ï¼‰ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºåœ¨å¢å¼ºå‹æ¨¡å¼ä¸‹ï¼Œå¯¼é€šç”µé˜»ä¼šæ˜¾è‘—å¢åŠ ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸ºè¿™æ˜¯å¦ä¸€ä¸ªå…³é”®æ–¹é¢ã€‚å¦å¤–ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬éœ€è¦è€ƒè™‘å¢å¼ºå‹æ–¹æ¡ˆä¸­çš„åå‘ä¼ å¯¼ï¼Œè¿™ç§æ–¹æ¡ˆåœ¨é«˜è¾¾ 8 è‡³ 8 ä¼çš„é«˜å‹ä¸‹å¾ˆå®¹æ˜“å‘ç”Ÿï¼Œè€Œåœ¨ Cascode æ–¹æ³•ä¸­ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬åŸºæœ¬ä¸Šèƒ½å¤Ÿåƒæ ‡å‡†äºŒæç®¡ä¸€æ ·æä¾› 1 ä¼çš„ç”µå‹ã€‚æ‰€æœ‰è¿™äº›å› ç´ éƒ½ä¼šå½±å“åˆ°æ›´ä½åŠŸç‡ï¼Œå› ä¸ºâ€‹â€‹ä½ç”µå‹çš„å½±å“è¾ƒå°ã€‚å› æ­¤ï¼Œ[emode] å½“ç„¶å¾ˆæœ‰å¸å¼•åŠ›ï¼Œå› ä¸ºå®ƒçš„å¤æ‚æ€§è¾ƒä½ï¼Œå½“ç„¶ï¼Œå› ä¸ºæˆ‘ä»¬åœ¨ Cascode æ–¹æ¡ˆä¸­é‡‡ç”¨äº†èŠ¯ç‰‡çº§èŠ¯ç‰‡ (Chip-on-Chip) è§£å†³æ–¹æ¡ˆã€‚å› æ­¤ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬ä¹Ÿçœ‹åˆ°äº†å¢å¼ºå‹æ–¹æ¡ˆçš„ä»·å€¼ï¼ŒåŸºæœ¬ä¸Šæˆ‘ä»¬é‡‡ç”¨äº†ä¸¤ç§æŠ€æœ¯æ¥è§£å†³æ•´ä¸ªåŠŸç‡å’Œç”µå‹èŒƒå›´çš„é—®é¢˜ã€‚

æˆ‘ï¼šå¾ˆå¥½ã€‚é‚£ä¹ˆï¼Œç°åœ¨è°ˆè°ˆæˆæœ¬ã€æ¶æ„ã€åˆ¶é€ å’Œå¯é æ€§ã€‚éšç€GaNæŠ€æœ¯çš„å‘å±•ï¼Œè¿›å†›é«˜å¯é æ€§å¸‚åœºï¼Œç›®å‰å¿…é¡»æ»¡è¶³å“ªäº›è¡Œä¸šæ ‡å‡†æˆ–è®¤è¯éšœç¢ï¼Ÿä½œä¸ºç‘è¨ç”µå­ï¼Œä½ ä»¬å¦‚ä½•ä¸ºå®šä¹‰é•¿æœŸå¯é æ€§æ•°æ®åšå‡ºè´¡çŒ®ï¼Ÿå› ä¸ºè¿™å¯¹åœ¨ä¸åŒé¡¹ç›®ä¸­è½¬å‘GaNå™¨ä»¶çš„ç”µæºå·¥ç¨‹å¸ˆæ¥è¯´éå¸¸é‡è¦ã€‚

æˆ‘ï¼šè°¢è°¢ï¼ŒPietroã€‚è¯´åˆ°å¯é æ€§ï¼Œæˆ‘æƒ³é—®ä¸€ä¸‹å°è£…æ–¹é¢çš„é—®é¢˜ã€‚å°è£…æ˜¯ç¬¬ä¸€ä¸ªå®¹æ˜“å¤±æ•ˆçš„ã€‚å¦‚æœæˆ‘ä»¬è°ˆè®ºå¯é æ€§ï¼Œé‚£ä¹ˆæˆ‘ä»¬è°ˆè®ºçš„æ˜¯åº”ç”¨ï¼Œåœ¨è¿™ç§æƒ…å†µä¸‹ä¹ŸåŒ…æ‹¬çƒ­æ€§èƒ½ã€‚æ¸©åº¦æ˜¯ä¸€ä¸ªé‡è¦å› ç´ ã€‚é‚£ä¹ˆï¼Œåœ¨å°è£…æ–¹é¢ï¼Œå“ªäº›åˆ›æ–°å¯ä»¥æé«˜GaNåœ¨é«˜åŠŸç‡åº”ç”¨ä¸­çš„å¯é æ€§ï¼Ÿæˆ‘ä»¬æ˜¯å¦éœ€è¦ä¸åŒçš„æ”¹è¿›å’Œå°è£…æ–¹é¢çš„è¿›æ­¥æ¥å……åˆ†å‘æŒ¥GaNå’Œæ™¶ä½“ç®¡çš„é«˜é€Ÿå¼€å…³èƒ½åŠ›ï¼Œå› ä¸ºè¿™æ˜¯GaNçš„ä¸»è¦å…ƒç´ ï¼Ÿ
